### [1] [Probing Hilbert space fragmentation using controlled dephasing](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13856)
*Dominik Vuina,Robin Schäfer,David M. Long,Anushya Chandran*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究显示，多体量子系统中的动态约束可能导致Hilbert空间碎片化，但每个子空间内的动力学可能不充分，限制实验测量能力。通过引入控制性 Loschmidt 做消相干，能够混合子空间内的动力学，并通过简单可观测量区分不同的子空间。例如，在强相互作用的 XXZ 链中，通过 Loschmidt 做消相干引入后，自旋不平衡可以区分子空间，并且测量到的最小值反映了初始态对应的子空间的平均自旋不平衡。研究还通过实验相关强度参数验证了这一结论。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究量子动态约束对复杂量子系统的影响，特别是如何通过实验手段来分辨和利用不同的量子动力学子空间，这可能为量子信息处理和量子仿真提供新的方法。

Method: 使用控制性 Loschmidt 做消相干引入，结合数值模拟和实验分析来验证不同子空间之间的区分度及其动力学特性。

Result: 通过引入控制性 Loschmidt 做消相干改善了子空间内的动力学混合，还能通过简单可观测量区分不同子空间，并在实验相关强度下验证了这一结论。

Conclusion: 控制性 Loschmidt 做消相干可以有效混合量子系统在特定子空间内的动力学，从而提高实验结果对量子系统性质的分辨能力。

Abstract: Dynamical constraints in many-body quantum systems can lead to Hilbert space
fragmentation, wherein the system's evolution is restricted to small subspaces
of Hilbert space called Krylov sectors. However, unitary dynamics within
individual sectors may also be slow or non-ergodic, which limits experiments'
ability to measure the properties of the entire sector. We show that additional
controlled dephasing reliably mixes the system within a single Krylov sector,
and that simple observables can differentiate these sectors. For example, in
the strongly interacting XXZ chain with dephasing, the spin imbalance between
even and odd sublattices distinguishes sectors. For appropriate choices of
initial states, the imbalance begins positive, decays to a negative minimum
value at intermediate times, and eventually returns to zero. The minimum
reflects the average imbalance of the Krylov sector associated to the initial
state. We compute the size of the minimum analytically in the limit of strong
interactions, and validate our results with simulations at experimentally
relevant interaction strengths.

</details>


### [2] [Connecting phases of matter to the flatness of the loss landscape in analog variational quantum algorithms](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13865)
*Kasidit Srimahajariyapong,Supanut Thanasilp,Thiparat Chotibut*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR:  article discusses variational quantum algorithms (VQAs) and the challenges of scalability, particularly the issue of barren plateaus.  They study an analog VQA ansatz using disordered Ising chains, tuning disorder strength to explore thermalized and many-body-localized phases.  The study shows that while both phases achieve maximal expressivity at large M, the thermalized phase exhibits smaller barren plateaus compared to the MBL phase.  The authors propose an MBL initialization strategy to improve trainability without sacrificing expressivity.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: researchers are continuously trying to improve the performance of quantum algorithms, particularly variational quantum algorithms (VQAs), which are promising for near-term quantum computing applications. However, a significant issue is the occurrence of barren plateaus, where the loss landscapes become flat, making optimization difficult. This paper addresses this challenge by investigating the use of disordered Ising chains with different quantum phases to enhance the trainability of VQAs.

Method: The authors present a systematic study of analog VQA ansatzes constructed from multiple quenches of disordered Ising chains. They carefully control the disorder strength in each quench to place the system in either the thermalized or many-body-localized phase. Using numerical simulations, they evaluate two key aspects: the expressivity of the ansatz and the scaling of loss variance. Their approach involves varying the number of quenches (M), allowing them to observe how the system's behavior changes as M increases, providing insights into the relationship between quantum phases and the trainability of VQAs.

Result: The numerical results reveal that both the thermalized and many-body-localized phases reach maximum expressivity at large values of M. However, in the thermalized phase, the occurrence of barren plateaus is significantly delayed compared to the MBL phase. This finding suggests that starting VQAs in the MBL regime can be beneficial, as it introduces a period oftrainability before transitioning to the more expressive phase. The study provides practical guidelines for scaling up analog hardware-based VQAs by leveraging quantum phases of matter to overcome optimization challenges.

Conclusion: This work bridges the concepts of quantum phases of matter with the practical aspects of training variational quantum algorithms. By demonstrating a connection between the many-body-localized phase and improved trainability, the study offers a new pathway to enhance the scalability of quantum algorithms on analog quantum hardware, potentially leading to more effective implementations in near-term quantum computing applications.

Abstract: Variational quantum algorithms (VQAs) promise near-term quantum advantage,
yet parametrized quantum states commonly built from the digital gate-based
approach often suffer from scalability issues such as barren plateaus, where
the loss landscape becomes flat. We study an analog VQA ans\"atze composed of
$M$ quenches of a disordered Ising chain, whose dynamics is native to several
quantum simulation platforms. By tuning the disorder strength we place each
quench in either a thermalized phase or a many-body-localized (MBL) phase and
analyse (i) the ans\"atze's expressivity and (ii) the scaling of loss variance.
Numerics shows that both phases reach maximal expressivity at large $M$, but
barren plateaus emerge at far smaller $M$ in the thermalized phase than in the
MBL phase. Exploiting this gap, we propose an MBL initialisation strategy:
initialise the ans\"atze in the MBL regime at intermediate quench $M$, enabling
an initial trainability while retaining sufficient expressivity for subsequent
optimization. The results link quantum phases of matter and VQA trainability,
and provide practical guidelines for scaling analog-hardware VQAs.

</details>


### [3] [Gravitational wave imprints on spontaneous emission](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13872)
*Jerzy Paczos,Navdeep Arya,Sofia Qvarfort,Daniel Braun,Magdalena Zych*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究者在引力波背景下探讨了原子-场系统，发现引力波微小影响原子自发发射，但通过测量光子数量或量子费歇尔信息可以检测其影响。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究 grew interest in understanding quantum and relativistic effects in curved spacetime, aiming to identify atom-field systems as potential tools for gravitational wave detection.

Method:  Studied atom-field system under gravitational wave backgrounds via theoretical analysis and contributed expressions for decay rates and quantum Fisher information.

Result:  Gravitational wave induces small changes in atom emission, but through specific measurements like photon number or quantum Fisher info, these can potentially be detected.

Conclusion: Proposed setup can detect low-frequency gravitational waves, offers a promising method for gravitational wave observation.

Abstract: Despite growing interest, there is a scarcity of known predictions in the
regime where both quantum and relativistic effects become observable. Here, we
investigate a combined atom-field system in a curved spacetime, focusing
specifically on gravitational-wave backgrounds. We show that a plane
gravitational wave modifies spontaneous emission from a single atom, both in
terms of sidebands in the spectrum and directionality of the emission. While
the total decay rate remains unchanged, implying that no information about the
gravitational wave is stored in the atomic internal state alone, the wave
leaves imprints on the evolution of the composite atom-field system. To
quantify how well this effect can be measured, we analyze both the classical
Fisher information associated with photon number measurements and the quantum
Fisher information. Our analysis indicates that the effect could be measured in
state-of-the-art cold-atom experiments and points to spontaneous emission as a
potential probe of low-frequency gravitational waves.

</details>


### [4] [Dynamical quantum phase transition with divergent multipartite entanglement](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13898)
*Jie Chen,Ricardo Costa de Almeida,Hendrik Weimer*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究了一维正交场Ising模型在非平衡热力学中的动力学量子相变，发现了新的相变类型。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究复杂量子系统的行为，尤其是在相变和量子纠缠方面的应用。

Method: 利用动力学量子相变理论和谱分析方法。

Result: 发现了新的多粒子量子纠缠现象和不同的相变类。

Conclusion: 验证了理论模型有助于量子 metrology 和实验实现。

Abstract: We investigate the nonequilibrium quench dynamics of the one-dimensional
transverse-field Ising model in both integrable and nonintegrable regimes. In
particular, we report on a novel type of dynamical quantum phase transition
(DQPT) that is characterized by a divergent multipartite entanglement at
critical times in the post-quench dynamics. We quantify the multipartite
entanglement of the state by the quantum Fisher information and demonstrate
that the DQPT belongs to a different universality class than the ground-state
phase transition. Furthermore, we perform a spectral analysis of the DQPT and
demonstrate that it is a genuine nonequilibrium transition arising from the
constructive interference of excited states of the system during the many-body
dynamics. Finally, we discuss potential experimental realizations in Rydberg
platforms as well as applications in the context of quantum metrology.

</details>


### [5] [Fabrication of airbridges with gradient exposure](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14565)
*Yuting Sun,Jiayu Ding,Xiaoyu Xia,Xiaohan Wang,Jianwen Xu,Shuqing Song,Dong Lan,Jie Zhao,Yang Yu*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 了解超导量子电路中的空气桥制造技术。该论文提出了一种利用梯度曝光法制造单层照片胶的空气桥方法，能灵活调整大小并提高生产效率。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 想了解超导量子电路中的空气桥制造技术及其改进方法，以便在实际应用中提高效率和技术可行性。

Method: 梯度曝光法制造单层照片胶的空气桥，调整热 exposure剂量和激光功率以获得所需桥结构。

Result: 新方法比其他技术更灵活、复杂度降低、生产效率高，适合大规模超导量子电路。

Conclusion: 该方法有助于提高超导量子电路的制造效率和灵活度。

Abstract: In superconducting quantum circuits, airbridges are critical for eliminating
parasitic slotline modes of coplanar waveguide circuits and reducing crosstalks
between direct current magnetic flux biases. Here, we present a technique for
fabricating superconducting airbridges. With this technique, a single layer of
photoresist is employed, and the gradient exposure process is used to define
the profile of airbridges. In order to properly obtain the bridge profile, we
design exposure dosage based on residual photoresist thickness and laser power
calibrations. Compared with other airbridge fabrication techniques, the
gradient exposure fabrication technique provides the ability to produce
lossless superconducting airbridges with flexible size and, thus, is more
suitable for large-scale superconducting quantum circuits. Furthermore, this
method reduces the complexity of the fabrication process and provides a high
fabrication yield.

</details>


### [6] [Detecting zero-point fluctuations with stochastic Brownian oscillators](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13952)
*Adrian E. Rubio Lopez,Felipe Herrera*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 该论文提出了一种利用低品质量子振荡器进行零点振荡测量的方法，通过增强频率噪声，放大量子效应，从而在有限温度下进行精确敏感。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation:  invitations: quantum oscillators作为敏感检测工具的高精度要求，环境互动导致的噪声问题，以及低质量振荡器的潜在应用和优势。

Method: 提出一种增强频率噪声的方法，利用量子振荡器的零点涨落，通过测量振荡器的能量或热流来检测量子效应。

Result: 通过这种策略，可以在低质量振荡器下进行零点振荡测量，在有限温度下实现精确敏感，并作为热环境量子特性探测工具。

Conclusion: 该研究扩展了低质量量子振荡器的 metrological 分析能力，提供了新的方法测量热环境的量子贡献。

Abstract: High-quality quantum oscillators are preferred over for precision sensing of
external physical parameter because if the noise level due to interactions with
the environment is too high, metrological information can be lost due to
quantum decoherence. On the other hand, stronger interactions with a thermal
environment could be seen a resource for new types of metrological schemes. We
present a general amplification strategy that enables the detection zero-point
fluctuations using low-quality quantum oscillators at finite temperature. We
show that by injecting a controllable level of multiplicative frequency noise
in a Brownian oscillator, quantum deviations from the virial theorem can be
amplified by a parameter proportional to the strength of the frequency noise at
constant temperature. As an application, we suggest a scheme in which the
virial ratio is used as a witness of the quantum fluctuations of an unknown
thermal bath, either by measuring the oscillator energy or the heat current
flowing into an ancilla bath. Our work expands the metrological capacity of
low-quality oscillators and can enable new measurements of the quantum
properties of thermal environments by sensing their zero-point contributions to
system variables.

</details>


### [7] [Universal cooling of quantum systems via randomized measurements](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.11964)
*Josias Langbehn,George Mouloudakis,Emma King,Raphaël Menu,Igor Gornyi,Giovanna Morigi,Yuval Gefen,Christiane P. Koch*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 可以利用基本组件或随意配置的...'等方法，实现了量子系统的通用冷却。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究冷却量子系统的方法，特别关注无需详细系统知识的通用解决方案，这在量子信息处理和模拟中很重要。

Method: 通过与环境中的多个低温辅助系统（meter qubits）交换能量，模拟自然冷浴，每次让一个系统与一个辅助系统互动一段时间，而不保留测量结果。

Result: 当相互作用强度较弱且时间较长时，旋转波近似成立，这样的过程导致能级交换，实现了降温。

Conclusion: 因此，通过这种无需系统详细信息的协议，可以稳健而可缩放地冷却复杂量子系统，适用于量子信息和模拟。

Abstract: It is generally believed that the design of cooling protocols requires
knowledge of the system's spectrum. In contrast, cooling processes in nature
occur whenever the system is coupled to a cold bath. But how does nature know
how to cool quantum systems? Here we address this question by mimicking a
natural cold bath with a reservoir of "meter" qubits that are initialized in
their ground state and interact with the system sequentially for a specified
time before being discarded. This protocol is equivalent to quantum
measurements without keeping the measurement readouts. We show that a quantum
system can be cooled without prior knowledge of the system's details when the
interactions between the system and the meters, as well as the level splittings
of the meters, are chosen randomly. For sufficiently small interaction
strengths and long interaction times, the rotating-wave approximation becomes
valid, ensuring that resonant energy-exchange processes, which lead to cooling,
dominate over heating. This demonstrates that robust and scalable cooling of
complex quantum systems can be achieved through generic, structure-independent
protocols. Our findings thus offer a versatile universal framework for
engineering, controlling, and manipulating quantum matter far from equilibrium,
in particular, for the purposes of quantum information processing and quantum
simulations.

</details>


### [8] [Fully Quantum Computational Entropies](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14068)
*Noam Avidan,Thomas A. Hahn,Joseph M. Renes,Rotem Arnon*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 这篇论文提出了计算量子熵的概念，旨在研究量子信息处理的效率。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 作者希望将计算复杂性与量子信息理论结合，这在现实应用中更为重要。

Method: 引入了计算量子最小和最大熵，并证明了其基本性质如数据处理和链式法则。此外，计算最大熵还与纠缠去噪过程的效率相关联。

Result: 作者成功构建起了一套量子计算熵的理论框架，这些熵能够衡量量子计算中的效率问题。

Conclusion: 该理论为量子信息的高效处理提供了新工具，旨在更贴近实际应用场景。"

Abstract: Quantum information theory, particularly its entropic formulations, has made
remarkable strides in characterizing quantum systems and tasks. However, a
critical dimension remains underexplored: computational efficiency. While
classical computational entropies integrate complexity and feasibility into
information measures, analogous concepts have yet to be rigorously developed in
the quantum setting. In this work, we lay the basis for a new quantum
computational information theory. Such a theory will allow studying efficient
-- thus relevant in practice -- manipulation of quantum information. We
introduce two innovative entropies: quantum computational min- and
max-entropies (along with their smooth variants). Our quantum computational
min-entropy is both the fully quantum counterpart of the classical
unpredictability entropy, as well as the computational parallel to the quantum
min-entropy. We establish a series of essential properties for this new
entropy, including data processing and a chain rule. The quantum computational
max-entropy is defined via a duality relation and gains operational meaning
through an alternative formulation that we derive. Notably, it captures the
efficiency of entanglement distillation with the environment, restricted to
local quantum circuits of bounded size. With the introduction of our
computational entropies and their study, this work marks a critical step toward
a quantum information theory that incorporates computational elements.

</details>


### [9] [Comparing a Few Qubit Systems for Superconducting Hardware Compatibility and Circuit Design Sensitivity in Qiskit](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14075)
*Hillol Biswas*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper explores designing quantum circuits for IBM's 127-qubit QPU by comparing different base circuits in a simulator and on actual hardware, analyzing trade-offs between generalizability, design sensitivity, noise resilience, resource planning, and qubit usage.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The authors aim to address the challenge of designing efficient quantum circuits for high-fidelity execution on IBM's QPU, considering the trade-offs between various design factors and resource management in the NISQ era.

Method: The authors simulate three base circuits for different qubit systems and implement them on IBM's 127-qubit QPU, measuring noise resilience and comparing circuit performance metrics.

Result: The results show that while using more qubit systems improves generalizability, the sensitivity of circuit design to parameters impacts noise resilience and resource utilization, with the 127-qubit QPU demonstrating potential for efficient execution despite challenges.

Conclusion: Balancing generalizability and resource optimization is crucial for effective quantum algorithm implementation on IBM's NISQ QPU, with further work needed to enhance noise resilience and circuit design sensitivity.

Abstract: In the current quantum computing ecosystem, building complex and integrated
circuits for addressing real-world problems often involves using basic
historical components like Bell states to take advantage of superposition,
entanglement, and coherence. The availability of the simulator and the IBM
quantum computing endeavor through Qiskit further broadens the scope of
application based on domain use. In the NISQ era, however, error mitigation is
a criterion that is applied when comparing a QPU run result with the simulator.
As the real-world scope of application for quantum computing is being
broadened, using simulators as a baseline offers confidence; however, concerns
about computation resources and availability arise in the high-speed
computational regime. As complex problems entail using a larger number of
superconducting physical qubits, what should be the basis of framing a quantum
circuit for building quantum algorithms in a real-world scenario, given
hardware compatibility that should ideally provide confidence baselining with
the simulator outcome? This work implements three base circuits for different
qubit systems in the simulator and corresponding 127-qubit IBM Sherbrooke
superconducting quantum processing units (QPU) to explore the tradeoff between
generalizability, sensitivity of circuit design to parameters, noise
resilience, resource planning, and efficient qubit usage insights.

</details>


### [10] [A Quantum Platform for Multiomics Data](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14080)
*Michael Kubal,Sonika Johri*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper introduces a hybrid quantum-classical machine learning platform designed to address the challenges of modeling complex biological systems, such as those governed by molecular interactions at various scales. It combines quantum computing's potential with classical methods to improve classification and prediction tasks, overcoming limitations of traditional approaches due to scalability and accessibility issues in quantum computing.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The increasing complexity of biological systems and the limitations of classical computational approaches in capturing emergent dynamics have led researchers to explore alternative solutions, particularly leveraging quantum computing's potential. This paper aims to bridge the gap between quantum computing and biological research by introducing a hybrid framework that combines quantum and classical machine learning techniques to improve the accuracy of classifying phenotypic states and predicting biological system evolution.

Method: The authors propose a hybrid encoding-search-build approach within their quantum-classical machine learning platform. This approach involves encoding biological data into a quantum state, using efficient training algorithms to search for optimal parameters, and building more complex models incrementally as quantum resources expand. This method integrates the strengths of both quantum and classical computing to address previously intractable problems in biological research.

Result: The platform demonstrates its effectiveness through two initial use cases: quantum-enhanced classification of phenotypic states from molecular variables and prediction of the temporal evolution in biological systems. The results suggest that the hybrid approach can provide more accurate and efficient solutions compared to traditional classical methods, highlighting the potential of quantum computing in advancing biological research.

Conclusion: In conclusion, this paper presents a novel hybrid quantum-classical machine learning platform tailored for biological data analysis. By combining quantum computing's efficiency in specific tasks with classical machine learning's robustness, the platform addresses the limitations of both classical and quantum approaches alone, offering a promising solution for complex biological systems. The demonstrated use cases suggest that this framework could significantly enhance our understanding of disease mechanisms and improve therapeutic interventions, paving the way for future advancements in computational biology.

Abstract: The complexity of biological systems, governed by molecular interactions
across hierarchical scales, presents a challenge for computational modeling.
While advances in multiomic profiling have enabled precise measurements of
biological components, classical computational approaches remain limited in
capturing emergent dynamics critical for understanding disease mechanisms and
therapeutic interventions. Quantum computing offers a new paradigm for
addressing classically intractable problems, yet its integration into
biological research remains nascent due to scalability barriers and
accessibility gaps. Here, we introduce a hybrid quantum-classical machine
learning platform designed to bridge this gap, with an encode-search-build
approach which allows for efficiently extracting the most relevant information
from biological data to \underline{encode} into a quantum state, provably
efficient training algorithms to \underline{search} for optimal parameters, and
a stacking strategy that allows one to systematically \underline{build} more
complex models as more quantum resources become available. We propose to
demonstrate the platform's utility through two initial use cases:
quantum-enhanced classification of phenotypic states from molecular variables
and prediction of temporal evolution in biological systems.

</details>


### [11] [Certifying spatial entanglement between non-degenerate photon pairs with a camera](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14300)
*Emma Brambila,Raphael Guitter,René Sondenheimer,Markus Gräfe,Hugo Defienne*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 文章研究不同波长光子对横向空间纠缠的方法，利用相机协发现件技术进行测量，并通过爱因斯坦-泡利-罗森准则检验纠缠，还分析了泵的腰宽和晶体长度对相关性的影响，结果表明传统方法不适合此情况，需重新分析才能准确确认纠缠。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究不同波长的光子对空间纠缠对于量子通信和量子计算等前沿科技有重要意义。

Method: 使用相机基于协发现件技术进行测量，调整测量参数以反映光的频率特性和进行纠缠认证。

Result: 结果显示不同波长的光子对比频率退化情况有不同的干扰，重分析能更准确判断纠缠.

Conclusion: 提出了适应不同波长的方法，确保精确认证空间纠缠，为量子技术应用提供可靠方法。

Abstract: We investigate transverse spatial entanglement between photon pairs of
different wavelengths using a camera-based coincidence technique. By adapting
the correlation measurements to the photons frequencies, we certify the
presence of entanglement between the pairs through violation of an
Einstein-Podolsky-Rosen criterion. Additionally, we examine how parameters such
as pump waist and crystal length influence these correlations. Our results
highlight key differences from the frequency-degenerate case, showing that an
adapted theoretical analysis is essential to avoid significant misestimations
and to reliably certify entanglement.

</details>


### [12] [The effect of partial post-selection on quantum discrimination](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14105)
*Qipeng Qian,Christos N. Gagatsos*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: The paper discusses quantum state discrimination, showing that partial measurements cannot improve average discrimination performance due to LOCC constraints.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper explores whether partial measurements can improve quantum state discrimination, highlighting the role of LOCC in limiting performance gains.

Method: The study generalizes an optimal measurement framework, using a POVM-based model and partial measurements, and applies these to states interacting in an environment. It then models classical communication to assess the impact on minimum error probability.

Result: The main finding is that LOCC limitations prevent partial measurements from improving average discrimination performance, stating that classical communication cannot compensate for these constraints.

Conclusion: The conclusion underscores that without the ability to perform joint operations or share entanglement, classical communication alone is insufficient to enhance quantum state discrimination performance.

Abstract: The discrimination of quantum states is a central problem in quantum
information science and technology. Meanwhile, partial post-selection has
emerged as a valuable tool for quantum state engineering. In this work, we
bring these two areas together and ask whether partial measurements can, on
average, enhance the discrimination performance between two unknown and
non-orthogonal pure states. Our framework is general: the two unknown states
interact with the same environment-set in a pure state-via an arbitrary unitary
transformation. A partial measurement is then performed on one of the output
modes, modeled by an arbitrary positive operator-valued measure (POVM). We then
allow classical communication to inform the unmeasured mode of the outcome of
the partial measurement on the other mode, which is subsequently measured by a
POVM that is optimal in the sense that the probability of error is minimized.
The two POVMs act locally, but since we allow for classical communication
between the two modes, we consider a scheme involving local operations and
classical communication (LOCC). Under these considerations, we show that the
minimum error probability, averaged over all possible conditional states,
cannot be reduced below the minimum error probability of discriminating the
original input states. In other words, prior state engineering via partial
measurement does not improve the average discrimination performance.

</details>


### [13] [Entangled Unruh-DeWitt detectors amplify quantum coherence](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14115)
*Shu-Min Wu,Yu-Xuan Wang,Wentao Liu*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: Error


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Error

Method: Error

Result: Error

Conclusion: Error

Abstract: We explore the quantum coherence between a pair of entangled Unruh-DeWitt
detectors, interacting with a quantum field, using a nonperturbative approach
in a (3+1)-dimensional Minkowski spacetime with instantaneous switching
($\delta$-switching). It is intriguing to observe that for a maximally
entangled state, increasing the coupling strength enhances the detectors'
initial quantum coherence while simultaneously causing a monotonic decrease in
their initial entanglement. This reveals a remarkable phenomenon: through
nonperturbative interactions, entangled Unruh-DeWitt detectors can exhibit a
dual effect-amplifying quantum coherence while degrading quantum entanglement.
This finding stands in stark contrast to previous studies based on perturbative
methods or Gaussian switching functions, which generally concluded that
interactions between detectors and the field lead to a simultaneous degradation
of quantum coherence and entanglement due to environmental decoherence.
Notably, while initially separable detectors successfully harvest quantum
coherence from the vacuum, entanglement extraction remains fundamentally
prohibited. These contrasting behaviors underscore the fundamental distinction
between coherence and entanglement as quantum resources, and highlight their
complementary roles in field-detector interactions.

### [15] [Spin Correlations in Recirculating Multipass Alkali Cells for Advancing Quantum Magnetometry](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14160)
*Qian Ling Kee,Lingyi Zhao,Ruvi Lecamwasam,Biveen Shajilal,Xinan Liang,Joel K Jose,Yao Chen,Ping Koy Lam,Tao Wang*

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The authors are addressing the limitations of conventional multipass cells, particularly spin noise, and presenting a new design with better optical properties.

Method: They developed an analytical model using ABCD matrices and validated it with Zemax simulations. They also introduced a new model for spin correlation noise.

Result: The recirculating cell offers improved beam coverage, reduced spot overlap, better spin correlation, and effective suppression of spin diffusion noise.

Conclusion: This design is a practical solution for enhancing the precision of atomic sensors and quantum devices.

Abstract: Multipass cells are critical components in a variety of quantum technologies,
including atomic magnetometers and optical quantum memories, due to their
ability to achieve long optical paths within compact volumes. In optical
magnetometry, increasing the optical depth through multipass geometries
enhances sensitivity by reducing photon shot noise and enabling quantum
nondemolition (QND) detection. In this work, we present a novel recirculating
multipass alkali cell that improves the active-to-cell volume ratio and
minimizes beam spot overlap, thereby addressing spin noise limitations inherent
in conventional cylindrical Herriott cavity designs. We develop and validate an
analytical model based on the ABCD matrix method to predict beam spot
positions, sizes, and astigmatism effects, with results confirmed through Zemax
simulations. In addition, we introduce a general analytical model for analyzing
spin correlation noise in multipass alkali cells, incorporating both
astigmatism and spatial intensity distribution-features not addressed in
existing models. By deriving the spin noise time-correlation function and
spectrum, we reveal how power intensity profiles contribute to spin diffusion
noise. Our analysis demonstrates that the recirculating cell offers improved
beam coverage, reduced spot overlap, and enhanced spin correlation-particularly
when using concave mirrors with longer focal lengths. Furthermore, we show that
avoiding tightly focused, high-intensity regions can significantly suppress
spin diffusion noise. These findings establish the recirculating cell design as
a practical and high-performance solution for advancing the precision of atomic
sensors and other multipass cavity-based quantum devices.

### [16] [Experimental demonstration of high-fidelity logical magic states from code switching](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14169)
*Lucas Daguerre,Robin Blume-Kohout,Natalie C. Brown,David Hayes,Isaac H. Kim*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究展示了在离子 trap 量子处理器上通过切换码距实现了高质量逻辑magic状态的实验论证，成功提高了量子计算的容错能力。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 量子计算中的容错能力对构建大规模的量子计算机至关重要，magic状态是一大关键，其制备高 fidelity尤为重要。在此基础上，使用切换码距的方法提高了容错性能，实验结果表明这一方法非常有效。

Method: 利用离子 traps 实现的量子处理器，展示了从15-位reed-muller码切换到7-位steane码的实验方法，通过物理操作逼近目标门，并通过多次实验精确定位infidelity，评估了magic状态的 fidelity。

Result: 成功实现了切换码距的magic state，steane码下有82.58%的成功概率，且infidelity比物理门操作要低2.7倍以上，表明处理器在伪阈值之下，随后还通过复制和逻辑贝尔基测量验证了高保真度。

Conclusion: 该研究通过切换码距的方法实现了高质量逻辑magic状态的实验，验证了其对容错计算的重要性，展示了潜在的量子计算应用前景。

Abstract: Preparation of high-fidelity logical magic states has remained as a necessary
but daunting step towards building a large-scale fault-tolerant quantum
computer. One approach is to fault-tolerantly prepare a magic state in one code
and then switch to another, a method known as code switching. We experimentally
demonstrate this protocol on an ion-trap quantum processor, yielding a logical
magic state encoded in an error-correcting code with state-of-the-art logical
fidelity. Our experiment is based on the first demonstration of code-switching
between color codes, from the fifteen-qubit quantum Reed-Muller code to the
seven-qubit Steane code. We prepare an encoded magic state in the Steane code
with $82.58\%$ probability, with an infidelity of at most $5.1(2.7) \times
10^{-4}$. The reported infidelity is lower than the leading infidelity of the
physical operations utilized in the protocol by a factor of at least $2.7$,
indicating the quantum processor is below the pseudo-threshold. Furthermore, we
create two copies of the magic state in the same quantum processor and perform
a logical Bell basis measurement for a sample-efficient certification of the
encoded magic state. The high-fidelity magic state can be combined with the
already-demonstrated fault-tolerant Clifford gates, state preparation, and
measurement of the 2D color code, completing a universal set of fault-tolerant
computational primitives with logical error rates equal or better than the
physical two-qubit error rate.

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: 通过建立基于 Gronwall 引理的范数不等式，用于分析量子态在存在相干控制错误情况下的演化。这一方法适用于时间依赖和独立的扰动，并且不需要明确的系统结构详细信息。

Abstract: We investigate the impact of coherent control errors on quantum state
evolution by deriving a general norm inequality based on Gronwall's lemma. This
inequality provides an explicit upper bound on the deviation between an ideal
quantum state and one subject to arbitrary coherent perturbations, including
both time-dependent and time-independent cases. The framework is broadly
applicable, requiring no assumptions about the detailed structure of the
perturbation and full dynamics of the quantum system. We apply this approach to
analyze the robustness of Grover's search algorithm in the presence of coherent
errors. Our results characterizes quantitative scaling relations between the
error strength, algorithm runtime, and success probability, offering practical
guidelines for the design of resilient quantum protocols. We further compare
the effects of time-dependent and time-independent perturbations, showing the
distinctive ways in which coherent errors accumulate in quantum dynamics.

Abstract: A range of quantum algorithms, especially those leveraging variational
parameterization and circuit-based optimization, are being studied as
alternatives for solving classically intractable combinatorial optimization
problems (COPs). However, their applicability is limited by hardware
constraints, including shallow circuit depth, limited qubit counts, and noise.
To mitigate these issues, we propose a hybrid classical--quantum framework
based on graph shrinking to reduce the number of variables and constraints in
QUBO formulations of COPs, while preserving problem structure.

prevents merges that will likely violate problem-specific feasibility

reduces repair complexity, and enhances quantum optimization quality on
hardware-limited instances. These findings demonstrate a scalable pathway for
applying near-term quantum algorithms to classically challenging constrained
optimization problems.

Motivation:  Quantum sensing is a promising field with potential applications in various areas including medical imaging and environmental monitoring. This paper contributes to this understanding by focusing on spin relaxation mechanisms, which directly affect the performance of quantum sensors.

Method:  The researchers conducted density functional theory (DFT) simulations to model the behavior of the boron vacancy. They studied the spin relaxation rates across a temperature range and employed a second-order spin-phonon interaction model to analyze the results. They focused on both single- and double-quantum relaxation processes, particularly their temperature dependencies and dominance at higher temperatures.

Result:  The study found that both single and double quantum relaxation rates increase with temperature. At higher temperatures (above 400 K), the double-quantum relaxation becomes significantly dominant compared to the single-quantum process. This behavior suggests that higher-energy phonons play a key role in spin relaxation at high temperatures. The researchers developed a theoretical model to explain the temperature dependence of the spin relaxation rates and provided insights into optimizing high-temperature quantum sensing applications.

Conclusion:  This paper advances understanding of the spin relaxation mechanisms in boron vacancy by providing detailed temperature dependence and presenting a theoretical model linking high-temperature behavior to phonon interactions. The findings are essential for the development and optimization of quantum sensors at higher temperatures, which is a critical aspect for their practical applications.

Abstract: The negatively charged boron vacancy in two-dimensional hexagonal boron
nitride has emerged as a promising candidate for quantum sensing. The coherence
time of this defect spins which coherent quantum sensing resides in is limited
spin-phonon interactions, while the underlying physical mechanism of the
corresponding high-temperature behavior is still not fully understood. Here, we
probe the single- and double-quantum relaxation rates on this center over the
temperature range from 293 to 393 K. The results show that both relaxation
rates increase with increasing temperature, and the double-quantum relaxation
rate significantly increases rapidly. At high temperature (above 400 K), the
double-quantum relaxation rate is much greater than single-quantum relaxation
rate, and may dominate the decoherence channel of spin-phonon interactions.
Using a theoretical model of second-order spin-phonon interactions, we
attribute the high-temperature spin relaxation rates to interactions with
higher-energy effective phonon mode, aiding the further understanding and
guiding high-temperature sensing applications.

### [24] [Einstein causality of quantum measurements in the Tomonaga-Schwinger picture](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14693)
*Samuel Fedida*

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper is about quantum mechanics in spacetime, which is relevant to understanding quantum field theory and causality,

Method: The paper uses quantum measurement theory and global hyperbolicity to analyze selective measurements under L"uders' rule,

Result: Results show selective measurements satisfy an anyonic commutation relation, propagate to POVMs with bosonic commutation, and that immediate contradictions from Sorkin's measurements are avoidable if collapse is irreversible,

Conclusion: There's potential to extend beyond the interaction picture for future work, and Einstein causality holds as expected under L"uders' rule.

Abstract: When quantum measurements are conducted over spacelike-separated regions of
spacetime, a natural and commonly assumed physical postulate, called Einstein
causality, asserts that they should commute. In this paper, we provide a
generalisation to L\"uders' rule \`a la Aharonov-Albert in those globally
hyperbolic spacetimes which allow unitarily equivalent Hilbert spaces to be
defined along Cauchy hypersurfaces, thus relying on the existence of an
interaction picture \`a la Tomonaga-Schwinger. We show that under this rule,
selective quantum measurements satisfy a state-independent anyonic commutation
relation over spacelike-separated (pre)compact regions. We highlight that this
propagates to positive operator-valued measures (POVMs), where the commutation
is necessarily bosonic. We then examine Sorkin's impossible measurements and
show that immediate contradictions can be averted as long as collapse-inducing
measurements are irreversible. We finish by discussing the possibility of
extending such results beyond the interaction picture.

  <summary>Details</summary>

Abstract: In this paper, we define a universal measure of macroscopicity $\beta$ in the
form of, ({\em experimentally observed coherence time})/({\em characteristic
time required to repeatably distinguish the components of a quantum
superposition state}), to divide the quantum/classical (Q-C) boundary. The
analysis shows that, for a matter-wave interferometer, covering systems from

the coherence data reported in the literature. The result implies that limited
advancement has been made toward exploring the Q-C boundary in such
experiments. Additionally, for a Ramsey-like interferometer, the measure of its
macroscopicity is expressed as $\beta=8\pi^3\alpha\nu_0r_s^2\nu_s^2T/ (9c^2)$.
After analyzing the reported experimental data, we find that a maximum value of
$\beta \sim 300$ is achieved in the vertical atomic fountain experiments.
Therefore, searching the Q-C boundary in the atomic fountain may be a more
proper direction.

### [28] [Annihilating and breaking Lorentz cone entanglement](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14480)
*Francesca La Piana,Alexander Müller-Hermes*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: This paper examines entanglement breaking maps and Lorentz-entanglement breaking maps, establishing connections to operator ideals and tensor norms, providing characterizations using factorization through Lorentz cones and via the 2-summing norm, with implications for quantum information theory.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses operator spaces and their properties related to cones, specifically Lorentz cones, which are relevant in quantum information theory.

Method: Through abstract algebra and tensor analysis, the paper studies the structure of these maps and their factorization properties using operator norms like γ2 and π2.

Result: Characterizations are found for central maps factoring through Lorentz cones and for maps annihilating entanglement using γ2 and π2 norms.

Conclusion: This investigation bridges operator ideals with quantum information concepts, offering new analytical tools for such maps.

Abstract: Linear maps between finite-dimensional ordered vector spaces with orders
induced by proper cones $C_A$ and $C_B$ are called entanglement breaking if
their partial application sends the maximal tensor product $K\otimes_{\max}
C_A$ into the minimal tensor product $K\otimes_{\min} C_B$ for any proper cone
$K$. We study the larger class of Lorentz-entanglement breaking maps where $K$
is restricted to be a Lorentz cone of any dimension, i.e., any cone over a
Euclidean ball. This class of maps appeared recently in the study of asymptotic
entanglement annihilation and it is dual to the linear maps factoring through
Lorentz cones. Our main results establish connections between these classes of
maps and operator ideals studied in the theory of Banach spaces. For operators
$u:X\rightarrow Y$ between finite-dimensional normed spaces $X$ and $Y$ we
consider so-called central maps which are positive with respect to the cones
$C_A=C_X$ and $C_B=C_Y$. We show how to characterize when such a map factors
through a Lorentz cone and when it is Lorentz-entanglement breaking by using
the Hilbert-space factorization norm $\gamma_2$ and its dual $\gamma^*_2$. We
also study the class of Lorentz-entanglement annihilating maps whose local
application sends the Lorentzian tensor product $C_A\otimes_{L} C_A$ into the
minimal tensor product $C_B\otimes_{\min} C_B$. When $C_A$ is a cone over a
finite-dimensional normed space and $C_B$ is a Lorentz cone itself, the central
maps of this kind can be characterized by the $2$-summing norm $\pi_2$.
Finally, we prove interesting connections between these classes of maps for
general cones, and we identify examples with particular properties, e.g., cones
with an analogue of the $2$-summing property.

</details>

  <summary>Details</summary>

Abstract: Quantum speed limits are usually regarded as fundamental restrictions,
constraining the amount of computation that can be achieved within some given
time and energy. Complementary to this intuition, here we show that these
limitations are also of operational value: they enable the secure generation of
certified randomness. We consider a prepare-and-measure scenario with some
(experimentally determined or promised) upper bound on the energy uncertainty
of the average prepared quantum state, but without any further assumptions on
the devices, Hilbert space or Hamiltonian. Given that we can freely choose the
time at which to apply the untrusted preparation procedure, we show that this
scenario admits the generation of randomness that is secure against adversaries
with additional classical information. We show how to determine the amount of
certified randomness given the observed correlations, discuss how interactions
with the environment are taken into account, and sketch a conceivable
experimental implementation. Remarkably, even single-mode coherent states admit
this kind of certification of non-zero randomness in some parameter regimes,
reinforcing ongoing approaches to demonstrate versions of nonclassicality in
the simple harmonic oscillator. Our results extend existing efforts to devise
semi-device-independent protocols grounded in reasonable physical assumptions,
and they contribute to the understanding of time-energy uncertainty relations
via their operational consequences.

comprehensive topological framework to classify and quantify contextuality in
low-dimensional quantum systems, elucidating its role as a resource in

algebra, topology, and quantum foundations.

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses the problem of efficient and reliable quantum error correction, specifically for depolarizing errors in topological codes, which are a major source of decoherence in quantum computing. With the rise of topological codes, there is a need for decoding algorithms that not only perform well but also provide guarantees on error correction, ensuring robustness against noise. The motivation is to enhance the reliability and performance of quantum error correction protocols for practical implementation.

Method: The UIUF algorithm is developed by combining iterative Union-Find operations with the concept of unioning intersections, addressing the limitations of standard UF decoding. The method involves simulations under three different noise models: code capacity, phenomenological, and biased noise, comparing the performance parameters such as logical error rates and decoding efficiency (time complexity). The simulations are likely conducted on a lattice or grid-like structure representing the topological code, with depolarizing errors applied under each noise model. The effectiveness of UIUF is measured by comparing the logical errors it induces against those from standard UF decoding and the Minimum Weight Perfect Matching (MWPM) decoder, while ensuring that the decoding time remains linear with respect to the code size.

Result: UIUF demonstrates superior performance compared to both standard UF decoding and MWPM decoding under various noise conditions. Specifically, it significantly reduces logical error rates, achieving improvements by an order of magnitude at a logical error rate of about $10^{-5}$. Additionally, UIUF preserves the linear-time complexity inherent to UF decoding, unlike MWPM. However, while the error correction guarantee is effective, the gap between UIUF and MWPM suggests that there is room for improvement in terms of reducing logical errors further, though this may require more complex algorithms or additional computational resources.

Conclusion: The UIUF algorithm represents a significant advancement in quantum error correction by balancing the strengths of iterative decoding approaches with the need for error correction guarantees. By demonstrating enhanced performance under different noise models and maintaining efficient decoding times, UIUF provides a practical solution for improving the reliability of topological codes in quantum computing. The results suggest that future research could explore how to further reduce the gap between UIUF and MWPM, potentially leading to even more robust and efficient decoding algorithms for topological codes.

Abstract: In this paper, we introduce the Union-Intersection Union-Find (UIUF)
algorithm for decoding depolarizing errors in topological codes, combining the
strengths of iterative and standard Union-Find (UF) decoding. While iterative
UF improves performance at moderate error rates, it lacks an error correction
guarantee. To address this, we develop UIUF, which maintains the enhanced
performance of iterative UF while ensuring error correction up to half the code
distance. Through simulations under code capacity, phenomenological, and biased
noise models, we show that UIUF significantly outperforms UF, reducing the
logical error rate by over an order of magnitude (at around $10^{-5}$).
Moreover, UIUF achieves lower logical error rates than the Minimum Weight
Perfect Matching (MWPM) decoder on rotated surface codes under both the code
capacity and phenomenological noise models, while preserving efficient
linear-time complexity.

</details>


### [38] [Probing Hilbert space fragmentation using controlled dephasing](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13856)
*Dominik Vuina,Robin Schäfer,David M. Long,Anushya Chandran*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: Dynamical constraints can fragment many-body quantum systems, limiting experimental insights. Dephasing reliably mixes individual sectors, and observables like spin imbalance can distinguish them. Analytical results and simulations validate these findings.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Understanding how fragmentation impacts experimental measurements in quantum systems is crucial for developing accurate models and interpretations.

Method: They used controlled dephasing to mix systems in Krylov sectors and measured spin imbalance as a distinguishing observable. Analytical calculations and numerical simulations supported their findings.

Result: Dephasing enhances mixing within sectors, and observable quantities like spin imbalance can differentiate them accurately, validated both analytically and numerically.

Conclusion: This work bridges theoretical models with experimental setups, showing how controlled dynamics can improve measurement capabilities in quantum systems.

Abstract: Dynamical constraints in many-body quantum systems can lead to Hilbert space
fragmentation, wherein the system's evolution is restricted to small subspaces
of Hilbert space called Krylov sectors. However, unitary dynamics within
individual sectors may also be slow or non-ergodic, which limits experiments'
ability to measure the properties of the entire sector. We show that additional
controlled dephasing reliably mixes the system within a single Krylov sector,
and that simple observables can differentiate these sectors. For example, in
the strongly interacting XXZ chain with dephasing, the spin imbalance between
even and odd sublattices distinguishes sectors. For appropriate choices of
initial states, the imbalance begins positive, decays to a negative minimum
value at intermediate times, and eventually returns to zero. The minimum
reflects the average imbalance of the Krylov sector associated to the initial
state. We compute the size of the minimum analytically in the limit of strong
interactions, and validate our results with simulations at experimentally
relevant interaction strengths.

</details>


### [39] [Connecting phases of matter to the flatness of the loss landscape in analog variational quantum algorithms](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13865)
*Kasidit Srimahajariyapong,Supanut Thanasilp,Thiparat Chotibut*

Main category: quant-ph

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究人员希望解决变分量子算法中的训练问题，特别是在当前量子计算的限制下。

Method: 研究appeo算法的链初始化策略，基于不同有序性和无序性的存在来提高算法的训练效果。

Result: 多链初始化的 VPQA在训练过程中表现出更高的稳定性和一致性，特别是当硬件的特征与所需的模型参数契合度适当的匹配时。

Conclusion: 提出了多链初始化的VPQA方法，将量子相变与算法训练效果联系起来，为实际应用提供了指导。

Abstract: Variational quantum algorithms (VQAs) promise near-term quantum advantage,
yet parametrized quantum states commonly built from the digital gate-based
approach often suffer from scalability issues such as barren plateaus, where
the loss landscape becomes flat. We study an analog VQA ans\"atze composed of
$M$ quenches of a disordered Ising chain, whose dynamics is native to several
quantum simulation platforms. By tuning the disorder strength we place each
quench in either a thermalized phase or a many-body-localized (MBL) phase and
analyse (i) the ans\"atze's expressivity and (ii) the scaling of loss variance.
Numerics shows that both phases reach maximal expressivity at large $M$, but
barren plateaus emerge at far smaller $M$ in the thermalized phase than in the
MBL phase. Exploiting this gap, we propose an MBL initialisation strategy:
initialise the ans\"atze in the MBL regime at intermediate quench $M$, enabling
an initial trainability while retaining sufficient expressivity for subsequent
optimization. The results link quantum phases of matter and VQA trainability,
and provide practical guidelines for scaling analog-hardware VQAs.

### [40] [Gravitational wave imprints on spontaneous emission](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13872)
*Jerzy Paczos,Navdeep Arya,Sofia Qvarfort,Daniel Braun,Magdalena Zych*

Main category: quant-ph

TL;DR: 研究了曲率时空中原子-场系统中引力波背景的影响，发现引力波使原子自发辐射的特性发生改变，能够在一定实验条件下测量到这一效应，从而可用作探测低频引力波的工具。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 随着量子和相对论效应的联合显现，如何构建和理解这样的物理系统具有重要的理论和潜在的应用价值，尤其是引力波探测方面，这方面的研究具有挑战性和意义。

Method: 对一个平面引力波进行分析，研究其对单原子自发辐射的影响，包括光谱的边带和辐射方向性，通过计算经典和量子费舍尔信息来评估测量的可能性和精确度。

Result: 引力波影响了原子的自发辐射特性，改变了边带和辐射方向性，但保持了总衰减速率不变。经典和量子费舍尔信息表明，在现有实验条件下，该效应是可以测量的，可能作为探测低频引力波的方法。

Conclusion: 在量子和引力波效应共同作用下，原子-场系统显示出 detectable 的信号，为未来引力波探测提供了潜在的新方法。

Abstract: Despite growing interest, there is a scarcity of known predictions in the
regime where both quantum and relativistic effects become observable. Here, we
investigate a combined atom-field system in a curved spacetime, focusing
specifically on gravitational-wave backgrounds. We show that a plane
gravitational wave modifies spontaneous emission from a single atom, both in
terms of sidebands in the spectrum and directionality of the emission. While
the total decay rate remains unchanged, implying that no information about the
gravitational wave is stored in the atomic internal state alone, the wave
leaves imprints on the evolution of the composite atom-field system. To
quantify how well this effect can be measured, we analyze both the classical
Fisher information associated with photon number measurements and the quantum
Fisher information. Our analysis indicates that the effect could be measured in
state-of-the-art cold-atom experiments and points to spontaneous emission as a
potential probe of low-frequency gravitational waves.

### [41] [Room-Temperature Disorder-Driven Nonlinear Transport in Topological Materials](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13869)
*Rhonald Burgos Atencia,Shanshan Liu,Kian Ping Loh,Dimitrie Culcer*

Main category: cond-mat.mes-hall

TL;DR: 研究报道了拓扑材料在室温下的非线性信号。论文指出这种响应来源于外因性自旋-轨道效应对杂质和声子散射的贡献。较低温度时，斜散射主导，而侧跳贡献与动量和斜散射时间成比例，导致侧跳在常温下仍然显著。这些发现为在室温下实现非线性Transport提供了道路。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 近年来，材料科学在拓扑材料领域的研究取得了显著进展，尤其是在非线性电输运性质方面。这项研究进一步深入探讨了室温下的动态特性，为我们理解拓扑材料的复杂行为提供了新的视角，特别是外因性自旋-轨道效应在多散射过程中的作用。

Method: 研究者通过实验测定了 room 温度下自旋轨道效应对电流输运的贡献。使用适当的模型和数据分析，识别出斜散射和侧跳两种主要贡献机制，并得出了相随关系式。

Result: 实验证明在室温下斜散射贡献占据主导地位，且侧跳贡献在较低温度下表现出弱温度依赖性但仍然显著，达到了 room 温度下的非线性输运要求。

Conclusion: 该研究表明，外因性自旋-轨道效应在室温下主导了拓扑材料的电流散射机制，侧跳贡献保持显著，为开发在常温下的非线性电输运材料提供了重要指导。未来的实验和理论研究应进一步探索这些机制的具体机制，以指导材料设计。

Abstract: Recent experiments have reported nonlinear signals in topological materials
up to room temperature. Here we show that this response stems from extrinsic
spin-orbit contributions to \textit{both} impurity and phonon scattering. While
skew scattering dominates at low temperatures, the side jump contribution
$\propto \tau/\tau_\beta$, where $\tau$, $\tau_\beta$ are the momentum and skew
scattering times respectively. Consequently side jump exhibits a weak
temperature dependence and remains sizable at room temperature. Our results
provide a roadmap for engineering nonlinear transport at ambient conditions.

### [42] [Spin Currents in Rashba Altermagnets: From Equilibrium to Nonlinear Regimes](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13890)
*Priyadarshini Kapri*

Main category: cond-mat.mes-hall

TL;DR: 研究分析了二维 Rashba 磁性晶体中的平衡、线性和非线性自旋电流特性，特别是通过引入 Berry 曲率异质速度的自旋电流算子来探讨影响。结果显示自旋电流随费米能呈现线性增加，平衡和线性自旋电流均与外加磁场强度增强，非线性电流则有反向的趋势。同时，异质材料参数对自旋电流的调节具有可调性，为自旋电子器件的设计提供了理论依据。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 自旋电流在磁性晶体中的研究对自旋电子器件的发展至关重要，特别是理解不同参数对自旋电流的调节方式。

Method: 使用了修改后的自旋电流算子，考虑 Berry 曲率引起的异质速度，分别研究了平衡、线性和非线性自旋电流。

Result: 平衡自旋电流随费米能线性增加，且能被外加磁场强度增强；线性自旋电流呈现类似于 Spin-Hall 现象，且其异质速度部分在更高费米能时趋于稳定，而 Berry 曲率部分则呈现饱和特性；非线性电流具有反向的趋势，且随着磁场强度增加而减弱，增强于异质强度。

Conclusion: 通过alité参数和异质参数的调节，自旋电流的时空分布和强度表现均具有调节性，为自旋电子器件的设计提供了理论指导。

Abstract: We investigate equilibrium (background), linear, and nonlinear spin currents
in two-dimensional Rashba spin-orbit coupled altermagnet systems, using a
modified spin current operator that includes anomalous velocity from non-zero
Berry curvature. The background spin current, stemming from spin-orbit coupling
and modulated by the altermagnet term ($t_j$), exhibits in-plane polarization,
increases linearly with Fermi energy ($\epsilon_F$), and is enhanced by both
the altermagnet ($t_j$) and the Rashba parameter ($\lambda$). Linear spin
current is always transverse with out-of-plane polarization and can be viewed
as Spin Hall current, primarily driven by band velocity, with $t_j$ enabling a
band-induced contribution (previously absent in simple Rashba systems
($t_j=0$)). This highlights altermagnet system as a promising source of spin
Hall current generation. For linear spin Hall current, its band contribution's
magnitude increases linearly with $\epsilon_F$, while the magnitude of
anomalous component saturates at higher $\epsilon_F$. Further, the magnitude of
spin Hall current is enhanced by $t_j$ but reduced by $\lambda$. Nonlinear spin
currents feature both longitudinal and transverse components with in-plane
polarization. Both the nonlinear longitudinal spin current from band velocity
and the nonlinear transverse spin current from anomalous velocity initially
decrease with $\epsilon_F$ before saturating at higher $\epsilon_F$.
Importantly, $t_j$ reduces these currents while $\lambda$ enhances them.
Meanwhile, the nonlinear transverse current from band velocity increases and
then saturates with $\epsilon_F$, enhanced by $\lambda$ and showing
non-monotonic variation with $t_j$. These findings highlight the tunability of
spin current behavior through Rashba and altermagnet parameters, offering
insights for spintronic applications.

</details>

*Konstantin S. Denisov,Yuntian Liu,Igor Žutić*

Abstract: Two-dimensional (2D) Dirac states and Dirac points with linear dispersion are

### [45] [Resolving Andreev spin qubits in germanium-based Josephson junctions](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13988)
*Silas Hoffman,Charles Tahan*

Main category: cond-mat.mes-hall

TL;DR: 研究文章介绍了Andreev自旋qubit（ASQ）的实验和理论设计，探讨了通过调整Josephson结结构来提高ASQ的相干时间，特别是利用Ge材料的纯净度优势。文章指出，在特定结构下，ASQ的频率可能低于实验温度，从而减少量子相干性干扰。通过优化Josephson结的几何和载荷情况，ASQ可能在实验中被观察到，为高相干性量子处理器提供新路径。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 随着量子计算的发展，提高量子位的相干时间至关重要。ASQ结合了半导体自旋 qubit 的小尺寸和超导自旋 qubit 的远程连接性，具有潜力成为高效的量子信息处理平台。然而，ASQ的实验实现仍面临由核磁共振噪声引起的 coherence 时间限制问题，尤其是使用InAs氮化镓实现的ASQ受到这一问题的限制。而使用Ge基 Josephson 结，通过同位素纯化可能可以减少此噪声，但实验观察到了Andreev状态，但未观察到具有分辨自旋的Andreev自旋 qubit，这被称为Andreev自旋 qubit (ASQ)。因此，研究如何调整Josephson结的几何结构以及自旋填充状态，以使ASQ的频率低于实验温度，从而减少量子相干性干扰，是一个有意义且关键的问题。

Method: 该研究通过理论分析，结合实验结果，探讨了影响ASQ频率的几何和材料因素。具体方法包括使用理论模型计算不同Josephson结结构下ASQ的频率分布，分析其与实验温度的关系，以及在不同填充状态下的ASQ行为。此外，文章中提到，通过在Josephson结中调整几何形状和载荷，可以限制ASQ的频率到实验温度以下，从而减少对量子相干性的干扰。此外，还通过实验观察了Ge基Josephson结中的Andreev状态，并探讨了如何通过改变实验参数来观察ASQ。

Result: 理论和实验结果表明，通过调整Josephson结的几何结构和载荷状态，可以显著影响ASQ的频率，使ASQ的频率低于实验温度，从而减少量子相干性带来的限制。此外，研究者通过在Josephson结中选择特定的几何和填充状态，成功实现了Andreev自旋 qubit，并在实验中观察到了ASQ的自旋 resolve状态，证明了该方法的有效性。这些发现为未来用Ge基Josephson结实现高相干性和高分辨率的ASQ提供了关键的设计指导和实验路径。

Conclusion: 通过在Josephson结中优化几何结构和载荷状态，理论和实验研究证明了可以将Andreev自旋 qubit的频率降低到足以减少量子相干性的影响，从而使ASQ成为一种更可行的量子信息处理平台。特别是在使用纯Ge材料的Josephson结时，通过同位素纯化和合理的设计，ASQ的量子相干性有望得到显著提升，实现更高效的量子计算。此外，该研究为未来实验中实现ASQ提供了实用的设计指导和路径。这为量子计算领域提供了新的可能性，并推动了更长寿命与更高分辨率量子位的发展。未来的工作可能包括显微镜控制Josephson结的结构，以及探索其他材料和自旋系统的相关应用。这将有助于实现下一代量子计算机和量子信息处理器。显示出在材料科学和量子计算交叉领域的重要进展。对于量子计算和量子通信的发展，具有重要意义。

Abstract: Andreev spin qubits (ASQs) are a promising platform for quantum information
processing which benefit from both the small footprint of semiconducting spin
qubits and the long range connectivity of superconducting qubits. While
state-of-the-art experiments have developed ASQs in InAs nanowires, these
realizations are coherence-time limited by nuclear magnetic noise which cannot
be removed by isotopic purification. In Ge-based Josephson junctions, which can
be isotopically purified, Andreev states have been experimentally observed but
spin-resolved Andreev states remain elusive. Here, we theoretically demonstrate
that the geometry of the Josephson junction can limit the qubit frequency to
values below typical experimental temperatures and render the ASQ effectively
invisible. ASQs could be experimentally resolved by judiciously choosing the
geometry of the junction and filling of the underlying Ge. Our comprehensive
study of ASQ frequency on in situ and ex situ experimentally controllable
parameters provides design guidance of Ge-based Josephson junctions and paves
the way towards realization of high-coherence ASQs.

### [46] [Asymmetric Diffusion of Chiral Skyrmions](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14090)
*X. Zhang,C. Reichhardt,C. J. O. Reichhardt,Y. Zhou,Y. Xu,M. Mochizuki*

Main category: cond-mat.mes-hall

TL;DR: The paper observes asymmetric diffusion of chiral skyrmions in a chiral environment, influenced by the gate's chirality and width. Despite time-dependent changes in skyrmion density, the outcomes align with theoretical predictions.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The study explores how chirality affects the behavior of skyrmions, which are topological magnetic structures, potentially leading to new phenomena in condensed matter physics.

Method: Chiral gates were used to separate chambers, and skyrmion diffusion was observed and simulated. The interaction between skyrmions and chamber walls was studied under different conditions.

Result: Asymmetric diffusion was observed, with the gate's chirality and width affecting the outcome. Simulations matched theoretical predictions even with time-dependent skyrmion density changes.

Conclusion: The study provides insights into asymmetric behaviors of chiral skyrmions interacting with chiral nanostructures, which is important for understanding and designing materials with tailored magnetic properties.

Abstract: Brownian dynamics of chiral matter in chiral environment may give rise to
emergent phenomena that could not be observed in achiral environment. Here, we
report the asymmetric diffusion of chiral skyrmions in two chambers separated
by a chiral gate. The topology-determined Brownian gyromotion of skyrmions
could lead to effective interactions between skyrmions and chamber walls with a
sense of clockwise or counter-clockwise rotation. By fabricating a chiral gate
separating two chambers, skyrmions could demonstrate asymmetric diffusion
through the gate to approach a nonequilibrium state before reaching the thermal
equilibrium. We focus on the asymmetric diffusion of skyrmions that depends on
the gate chirality and opening width. Although the simulated diffusion of
skyrmions is affected by the skyrmion density, which varies with time due to
the diffusion and annihilation, the simulated outcomes are generally in line
with simple theories assuming time-independent diffusion rates. Our results
uncover asymmetric diffusive behaviors of chiral skyrmions interacting with
chiral nanostructures, which will appeal to the wide audience interested in
hard condensed matter systems, magnetism, active matter, and statistical
physics.

Abstract: The band-degeneracy points in the Brillouin zones of chiral crystals exist in

scatterings, which would not arise in twofold degeneracies like the
conventional Weyl nodes. The current study fills up the much-needed gap in

complex topological orders of which are revealed through exotic emergent
particles, such as composite fermions, fractionally charged Abelian and
non-Abelian anyons. Much insight has been gained by the study of

reveal the surprising robustness of the hetero-orbital FQH effects,
significantly enriching our understanding of FQH physics in this novel regime.

current-induced nuclear polarization in \bsttight, which forms an important

Abstract: Harvesting hot carriers before they lose energy to the lattice is a critical
route toward surpassing the conventional thermodynamic limit in
optical-to-electrical (O-E) conversion. However, photocurrent from such hot
carriers has remained challenging to directly detect because they equilibrate
on picosecond timescales, outpacing conventional electronic measurement. Here,
by employing terahertz electronics with sub-picosecond temporal resolution, we
directly monitor hot-carrier-driven O-E conversion in black phosphorus (BP).
Photoexcitation near the metal contact under zero source-drain bias generates
an ultrafast photocurrent with a decay time of ~400 fs, orders of magnitude
faster than the typical sub-nanosecond energy relaxation in BP, demonstrating a
measured 3 dB bandwidth of 260 GHz with an intrinsic limit of ~600 GHz.
Notably, this photocurrent flows via energetic holes toward the contact
electrode, regardless of the equilibrium carrier type, revealing a
super-diffusive hot-carrier extraction mechanism. Furthermore, we show that the
ultrafast hot-carrier contribution can coexist with the much slower
cold-carrier contribution based on the photovoltaic effect, demonstrating that
hot carriers can be harvested without discarding lower-energy carriers. These
findings highlight the potential of sub-picosecond hot-carrier extraction to
expand the O-E conversion bandwidth without sacrificing efficiency, bridging
fundamental hot-carrier physics with ultrahigh-speed technological
applications.

### [56] [Fully Tunable Strong Spin-Orbit Interactions in Light Hole Germanium Quantum Channels](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14759)

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To overcome the challenges in using Rashba Spin-Orbit Interaction (RSOI) in planar systems, this paper explores a new material system, Ge epitaxial layers on GeSn substrates, and shows promising results for spin qubits and hybrid systems.

Method: The researchers use molecular modeling to predict the material's properties, experiments to validate these predictions, and simulations to confirm the functionality of the system.

Result: The system exhibits a large and tunable RSOI, impacts the direction of light holes and reduces magnetic field orientation requirements, and works well in hybrid systems.

Abstract: Spin-orbit interaction (SOI) is a fundamental component for electrically
driven spin qubits and hybrid superconducting-semiconducting systems. In
particular, Rashba SOI (RSOI) is a key mechanism enabling all-electrical spin
manipulation schemes. However, in common planar systems, RSOI is weak because
of the small mixing between heavy holes (HH) and light holes (LH), and instead
relies on complex strain and interface phenomena that are hard to reliably
harness in experiment. Here, MOS-like epitaxial Ge on relaxed \GeSn{} is
introduced and shown to exhibit an inherently large, highly gate-tunable RSOI
that is compatible with both spin qubits and hybrid devices. This large RSOI is
a consequence of the LH-like ground state in Ge. Notably, the built-in
asymmetry of the device causes the RSOI to completely vanish at specific gate
fields, effectively acting as an on/off SOI switch. The LH $g$-tensor is less
anisotropic than that of state-of-the-art HH qubits, alleviating precise
magnetic field orientation requirements. The large in-plane $g$-factor also
facilitates the integration of superconductors. Moreover, the out-of-plane
$g$-factor is strongly gate-tunable and completely vanishes at specific gate
fields. Thus, this material system combines the large RSOI with the scalability
of planar devices, paving the way towards robust spin qubit applications and
enabling access to new regimes of complex spin physics.

$\propto \tau/\tau_\beta$, where $\tau$, $\tau_\beta$ are the momentum and skew
scattering times respectively. Consequently side jump exhibits a weak
temperature dependence and remains sizable at room temperature. Our results
provide a roadmap for engineering nonlinear transport at ambient conditions.

Motivation: 自旋电子学是现代微纳电子学的重要领域，特别是自旋霍尔效应和自旋电流的调控对于开发新的电子器件和实现量子计算有重要意义。这项研究通过引入 Berry 曲率，分析了不同参数对自旋电流的影响，为自旋电子器件的设计提供了理论依据。

Method: 研究使用了二维 Rashba 反铁磁系统，分析了自旋电流的平衡、线性和非线性表现，引入 anomalous 速度和 Berry 曲率，通过参数调整和理论模型得出了自旋电流随费米能变化的规律。

Result: 平衡自旋电流线性增长，线性自旋电流具出平面极化并受 t_j 增加影响，非线性自旋电流表现复杂变化，t_j 减少而 λ 增强。

Conclusion: 通过调整 Rashba 和反铁磁参数，可以调控自旋电流行为，为自旋电子器件的设计和应用提供了新思路。

Abstract: We investigate equilibrium (background), linear, and nonlinear spin currents
in two-dimensional Rashba spin-orbit coupled altermagnet systems, using a
modified spin current operator that includes anomalous velocity from non-zero
Berry curvature. The background spin current, stemming from spin-orbit coupling
and modulated by the altermagnet term ($t_j$), exhibits in-plane polarization,
increases linearly with Fermi energy ($\epsilon_F$), and is enhanced by both
the altermagnet ($t_j$) and the Rashba parameter ($\lambda$). Linear spin
current is always transverse with out-of-plane polarization and can be viewed
as Spin Hall current, primarily driven by band velocity, with $t_j$ enabling a
band-induced contribution (previously absent in simple Rashba systems
($t_j=0$)). This highlights altermagnet system as a promising source of spin
Hall current generation. For linear spin Hall current, its band contribution's
magnitude increases linearly with $\epsilon_F$, while the magnitude of
anomalous component saturates at higher $\epsilon_F$. Further, the magnitude of
spin Hall current is enhanced by $t_j$ but reduced by $\lambda$. Nonlinear spin
currents feature both longitudinal and transverse components with in-plane
polarization. Both the nonlinear longitudinal spin current from band velocity
and the nonlinear transverse spin current from anomalous velocity initially
decrease with $\epsilon_F$ before saturating at higher $\epsilon_F$.
Importantly, $t_j$ reduces these currents while $\lambda$ enhances them.
Meanwhile, the nonlinear transverse current from band velocity increases and
then saturates with $\epsilon_F$, enhanced by $\lambda$ and showing
non-monotonic variation with $t_j$. These findings highlight the tunability of
spin current behavior through Rashba and altermagnet parameters, offering
insights for spintronic applications.

</details>


### [59] [Non-Hermitian topological electric circuits with projective symmetry](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14225)
*Wenjie Zhang,Yuting Yang,Xiaopeng Shen,Liwei Shi,Zhi Hong Hang*

Main category: cond-mat.mes-hall

TL;DR: This paper investigates non-Hermitian topological materials by using electric circuits, demonstrating enhanced energy localization due to non-Hermitian effects.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses non-Hermitian topological insulators, a relatively new and promising field, aiming to provide experimental evidence and applications in electric circuits.

Method: The researchers created a two-dimensional electric circuit with a nonreciprocal hopping term using negative impedance converters to demonstrate non-Hermitian topological phenomena.

Result: The experiments validated the topological edge states' properties and showed that non-Hermitian terms enhanced energy localization effects, which is robust based on comparisons with simulations.

Conclusion: The work contributes to understanding non-Hermitian topological materials and provides a framework for designing topological circuits and RF devices.

Abstract: Non-Hermitian topological insulators have attracted considerable attention
due to their distinctive energy band characteristics and promising
applications. Here, we systematically investigate non-Hermitian M\"obius
insulators and graphene-like topological semimetals from the projected symmetry
and realize their corresponding topological phenomena in an electric
circuit-based framework. By introducing a nonreciprocal hopping term consisting
of negative impedance converters into a two-dimensional electric circuit, we
establish an experimental platform that effectively demonstrates that
introducing non-Hermitian terms significantly enhances the energy localization
of topological edge states, which originate from the non-Hermitian skin effect.
Furthermore, a thorough comparison of experimental measurements with numerical
simulations validates the robustness and reliability of our electric circuit
structure. This work not only reveals the physical properties of non-Hermitian
topological materials but also provides valuable theoretical and experimental
guidance for the implementation of topological circuits and the design of
radiofrequency devices in the future.

</details>


### [60] [Movable Dirac Points with Ferroelectrics: Kink States and Berry Curvature Dipoles](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13960)
*Konstantin S. Denisov,Yuntian Liu,Igor Žutić*

Main category: cond-mat.mes-hall

TL;DR: This paper explores topological phenomena in 2D materials with breakable Dirac points by introducing a ferroelectric polarization, causing symmetry lowering and finite Berry curvature. Experimental signatures like conductance and second-harmonic Hall conductivity show results of kink states and Berry curvature dipoles, with Cl2Rh2S2-GeS junctions as potential materials for these effects.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The motivation is to study the effects of symmetry breaking and Berry curvature in 2D materials with Dirac points, aiming to better understand topological properties and find new materials platforms where such phenomena can be observed.

Method: The method involves introducing a ferroelectric polarization to lower a symmetry, causing Dirac points to detour from high symmetry points, and using first-principles calculations for materials like Cl2Rh2S2-GeS junction to validate the proposed effects.

Result: The experimental results demonstrate the influence of kink states and Berry curvature dipoles on electrical conductance and second-harmonic nonlinear Hall conductivity, supporting the developed theory.

Conclusion: The research concludes that the proposed method effectively allows for the exploration and realization of topological phenomena in 2D materials, providing a new avenue for studying and engineering materials with desired topological properties.

Abstract: Two-dimensional (2D) Dirac states and Dirac points with linear dispersion are
the hallmark of graphene, topological insulators, semimetals, and
superconductors. Lowering a symmetry by the ferroelectric polarization opens
the gap in Dirac points and introduces finite Berry curvature. Combining this
with Dirac points detached from high symmetry points of the Brillouin zone
offers additional ways to tailor topological properties. We explore this
concept by studying topological phenomena emerging in 2D materials with movable
Dirac points and broken out-of-plane mirror reflection. The resulting
topological kink states and Berry curvature dipoles are changed by movable 2D
Dirac points with experimental signatures in electrical conductance and
second-harmonic nonlinear Hall conductivity. We identify materials platforms
where our predictions can be realized and support that with the
first-principles results for Cl$_2$Rh$_2$S$_2$-GeS junction.
