### [62] [High-fidelity collisional quantum gates with fermionic atoms](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14711)
*Petar Bojović,Timon Hilker,Si Wang,Johannes Obermeyer,Marnix Barendregt,Dorothee Tell,Thomas Chalopin,Philipp M. Preiss,Immanuel Bloch,Titus Franz*

Main category: cond-mat.quant-gas

TL;DR: This paper presents a successful demonstration of collisional entangling gates using fermionic atoms with high fidelity and long coherence times. They achieved this using an optical superlattice platform and quantum gas microscopy. The gates are a crucial component for quantum chemistry simulations, paving the way for scalable hybrid quantum simulators. The results highlight the potential of using fermionic atoms in quantum computing applications, particularly in maintaining key symmetries.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper explores the application of quantum computing using fermionic atoms, which is a promising area given the challenges in implementing qubit-based quantum computing. The ability to directly simulate electronic structures and strongly correlated quantum phases makes this research significant for advancing quantum chemistry and materials science.

Method: They used an optical superlattice to control fermionic atoms. They demonstrated collisional entangling gates with high fidelity and measured the coherence times of Bell states to be over 10 seconds using quantum gas microscopy. The method involved precise control over the atoms' motion and their interactions.

Result: The gates achieved a fidelity of up to 99.75% and a Bell state lifetime exceeding 10 seconds, demonstrating robust and long-lasting entanglement. The gates are essential building blocks for quantum chemistry simulations.

Conclusion: The demonstration of these gates using fermionic atoms opens new possibilities for scalable quantum simulators in quantum chemistry and beyond. The results suggest that fermionic atoms could be a viable platform for quantum computing, leveraging their intrinsic symmetries to maintain key properties essential for simulations.

Abstract: Quantum simulations of electronic structure and strongly correlated quantum
phases are widely regarded as among the most promising applications of quantum
computing. These simulations require the accurate implementation of motion and
entanglement of fermionic particles. Instead of the commonly applied costly
mapping to qubits, fermionic quantum computers offer the prospect of directly
implementing electronic structure problems. Ultracold neutral atoms have
emerged as a powerful platform for spin-based quantum computing, but quantum
information can also be processed via the motion of bosonic or fermionic atoms
offering a distinct advantage by intrinsically conserving crucial symmetries
like electron number. Here we demonstrate collisional entangling gates with
fidelities up to 99.75(6)% and lifetimes of Bell states beyond $10\,s$ via the
control of fermionic atoms in an optical superlattice. Using quantum gas
microscopy, we characterize both spin-exchange and pair-tunneling gates
locally, and realize a robust, composite pair-exchange gate, a key building
block for quantum chemistry simulations. Our results enable the preparation of
complex quantum states and advanced readout protocols for a new class of
scalable analog-digital hybrid quantum simulators. Once combined with local
addressing, they mark a key step towards a fully digital fermionic quantum
computer based on the controlled motion and entanglement of fermionic neutral
atoms.

</details>


### [63] [Quantum simulation of fermionic non-Abelian lattice gauge theories in $(2+1)$D with built-in gauge protection](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14747)
*Gaia De Paciani,Lukas Homeier,Jad C. Halimeh,Monika Aidelsburger,Fabian Grusdt*

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究量子模拟在规范理论中的应用，尤其是非阿贝尔 LGTs 的模拟，这对于粒子物理和量子计算都具有重要意义。

Method: 论文提出了一种基于离子杂化态的量子模拟方案，通过引入磁Zeeman效应和超交换作用保护规范对称性。同时，扩展到混合数字-模拟器以模拟更大规模的非阿贝尔 U(N) LGTs。

Result: 成功设计了大规模且精确的保护方法，并扩展到适用于更大规模的模拟器，为未来研究提供了基础。

Conclusion: 该方案为模拟非阿贝尔 LGTs 开辟了新途径，推动了量子模拟与粒子物理的结合。

Abstract: Recent advancements in the field of quantum simulation have significantly
expanded the potential for applications, particularly in the context of lattice
gauge theories (LGTs). Maintaining gauge invariance throughout a simulation
remains a central challenge, especially for large-scale non-Abelian LGTs with
dynamical matter, which are particularly complex in terms of engineering for
experiments. Gauge-symmetry breaking is inevitable in established rishon-based
schemes for alkaline-earth-like atoms (AELAs) and controlling the magnitude of
its effect is an open challenge. Here, we first construct a minimal model to
quantum simulate non-Abelian LGTs ensuring that the gauge constraints are met
and explicitly derive their unambiguous non-Abelian nature. Second, we present
a proposal for a novel gauge protection scheme using native interactions in
AELAs enabling the simulation of toy models of non-Abelian $U(2)$ LGTs with
dynamical fermionic matter in $(2+1)$ dimensions on large scales. Due to the
simplicity of the gauge protection mechanism, based on a Zeeman shift in
combination with superexchange interactions, our scheme can be naturally
included in other rishon-based quantum simulation protocols. Third, we extend
our approach to a fully scalable, hybrid digital-analog simulator for $U(N)$
LGTs based on Rydberg AELA with variable rishon number. The proposed general
mechanism for gauge protection provides a promising path towards the
long-awaited simulation of non-Abelian LGTs relevant to particle physics.

Abstract: Europium Oxide (EuO), a low carrier density local moment ferromagnet, shows a
wide variety of transport behaviour depending on preparative conditions. Some
samples have a moderate resistivity with a modest peak near $T_c$ while others
show a huge peak in resistivity followed by insulating high temperature
behaviour. These features have been known for decades and have been attributed
to the presence of magnetic polarons in a disordered background. Actual
attempts at a theory, however, reduce the problem either to a single trapped
electron or to an averaged picture where the spatial physics of polarons is
lost. The difficulty stems from having to handle electronic states in a
magnetically fluctuating, structurally disordered background. Via an explicit
real space calculation in two dimensions, we examine the interplay of disorder
induced localisation and magnetic polaron formation and show how the
resistivity trends in EuO could emerge from increasing impurity concentration.
We estimate the polaron size in the disordered medium, establish the presence
of a pseudogap near $T_c$, predict a crossover to incoherent, non Drude,
optical response with growing disorder and temperature, and track the polaron
`delocalisation' with increasing magnetic field.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 该研究是在材料科学和量子相变领域的重要探索，挑战当前对非线性Kondo效应和拓扑态相变的理解。

Abstract: A Chern metal is a two-dimensional metallic state of matter carrying chiral
edge states. It can emerge as a doped Chern insulator, but theoretical studies
have also predicted its emergence near a Kondo breakdown separating a metallic
chiral spin liquid and a heavy Fermi liquid in a frustrated lattice. To date,
the latter exotic scenario has not been realized. Here, we report the
observation of a Chern metal at the onset of the magnetic Kondo breakdown in a
frustrated moir\'e Kondo lattice--angle-aligned MoTe2/WSe2 bilayers. The state
is compressible and is manifested by a nearly quantized Hall resistance but a
finite longitudinal resistance that arises from a bad metallic bulk. The state
also separates an itinerant and a heavy Fermi liquid and appears far away from
the band inversion critical point of the material, thus ruling out its origin
from simply doping a Chern insulator. We demonstrate the presence of a chiral
edge state by nonlocal transport measurements and current-induced quantum
anomalous Hall breakdown. Magnetic circular dichroism measurements further
reveal a magnetization plateau for the Chern metal before a metamagnetic
transition at the Kondo breakdown. Our results open an opportunity for moir\'e
engineering of exotic quantum phases of matter through the close interplay
between band topology and Kondo interactions.

Result: 主要结果包括：在强相互作用下，SU(3) Hubbard模型实现了三子集 antiferromagnetic 阶序；在中间相互作用下，发现了具有不同长度Zigzag模式的antiferromagnetic 有序态；颜色有序参数和能量异质性在相变处出现不连续；通过能量贡献分析，确认了低能键在Zigzag态的稳定性。

Abstract: SU(N) Hubbard models exhibit a rich variety of phases, which may be realized
through quantum simulation with ultracold atomic gases in optical lattices. In
this work we study the Mott insulating phases of the SU(3) Hubbard model at

previously identified in the SU(3) Heisenberg model. At intermediate
interaction strength we find antiferromagnetic states exhibiting zigzag
patterns of different lengths, in agreement with previous Hartree-Fock and
constrained-path auxiliary-field quantum Monte Carlo calculations. We study the

Abstract: Europium Oxide (EuO), a low carrier density local moment ferromagnet, shows a
wide variety of transport behaviour depending on preparative conditions. Some
samples have a moderate resistivity with a modest peak near $T_c$ while others
show a huge peak in resistivity followed by insulating high temperature
behaviour. These features have been known for decades and have been attributed
to the presence of magnetic polarons in a disordered background. Actual
attempts at a theory, however, reduce the problem either to a single trapped
electron or to an averaged picture where the spatial physics of polarons is
lost. The difficulty stems from having to handle electronic states in a
magnetically fluctuating, structurally disordered background. Via an explicit
real space calculation in two dimensions, we examine the interplay of disorder
induced localisation and magnetic polaron formation and show how the
resistivity trends in EuO could emerge from increasing impurity concentration.
We estimate the polaron size in the disordered medium, establish the presence
of a pseudogap near $T_c$, predict a crossover to incoherent, non Drude,
optical response with growing disorder and temperature, and track the polaron
`delocalisation' with increasing magnetic field.

*Wenjin Zhao,Zui Tao,Yichi Zhang,Bowen Shen,Zhongdong Han,Patrick Knüppel,Yihang Zeng,Zhengchao Xia,Kenji Watanabe,Takashi Taniguchi,Jie Shan,Kin Fai Mak*

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: 使用了 kích resonance 覆하시 吳的双层莫里埃structure 材料，通過電磁argon等方法领导班子的特性，如 hall 阻礙、纵向阻抗等，並通過磁性圓 '<? envisioned 仏描寫具體實驗步驟和і具體 technique來分析 material 的 behavior.

Result:  research team 碹現了 Chern 金屬的 Hall 诊断特性，其 Hall 效应接近量⼦化，但具有有限的纵向阻抗，表明存在粗糙的带Edge的传导態，并 labour the presence of 電流induced quantum anomalous Hall 效应。 Corvette 参数 further hta甚為 magnetization plateaux 在 Chern 金屬之前出現, 个性化地指出了过渡的 Magnetic Kondo breakdown，表明这一态是通过 band topology 和 Kondo interactions的相互作用形成的。

Abstract: A Chern metal is a two-dimensional metallic state of matter carrying chiral
edge states. It can emerge as a doped Chern insulator, but theoretical studies
have also predicted its emergence near a Kondo breakdown separating a metallic
chiral spin liquid and a heavy Fermi liquid in a frustrated lattice. To date,
the latter exotic scenario has not been realized. Here, we report the
observation of a Chern metal at the onset of the magnetic Kondo breakdown in a
frustrated moir\'e Kondo lattice--angle-aligned MoTe2/WSe2 bilayers. The state
is compressible and is manifested by a nearly quantized Hall resistance but a
finite longitudinal resistance that arises from a bad metallic bulk. The state
also separates an itinerant and a heavy Fermi liquid and appears far away from
the band inversion critical point of the material, thus ruling out its origin
from simply doping a Chern insulator. We demonstrate the presence of a chiral
edge state by nonlocal transport measurements and current-induced quantum
anomalous Hall breakdown. Magnetic circular dichroism measurements further
reveal a magnetization plateau for the Chern metal before a metamagnetic
transition at the Kondo breakdown. Our results open an opportunity for moir\'e
engineering of exotic quantum phases of matter through the close interplay
between band topology and Kondo interactions.

universal. Superradiant amplification does not seem to trigger an instability

Abstract: While the third LIGO--Virgo gravitational-wave transient catalog includes 90
signals, it is believed that ${\cal O}(10^5)$ binary black holes merge
somewhere in the Universe every year. Although these signals are too weak to be
detected individually with current observatories, they combine to create a
stochastic background, which is potentially detectable in the near future.

(2017) showed that a vastly more sensitive ``coherent'' search can be carried

for a gravitational-wave background search with unprecedented sensitivity.

### [78] [Leading-order gravitational time delay of massive particles by a moving Schwarzschild lens](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14184)
*Guansheng He,Wenbin Lin,Yi Xie*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper presents a comprehensive analysis of the gravitational time delay caused by a moving Schwarzschild black hole, specifically for relativistic particles. The study introduces a unified formula that accounts for both massive and massless particles, employing a first post-Minkowskian approximation. The findings reveal that the radial motion of the lens significantly affects the travel time, with towards motion decreasing flight time and away motion increasing it compared to a stationary case. The paper concludes with an evaluation of the detectability of these effects using typical black holes as examples.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Understanding the effects of black hole motion on gravitational time delay is crucial for testing general relativity and has implications for high-energy physics and cosmology. This paper aims to provide a detailed analytical framework to model these effects accurately.

Method: The research employs the equations of motion in the spacetime generated by a moving Schwarzschild black hole. It uses the first post-Minkowskian approximation to derive a unified formula for travel times. Analytical expressions for the time delay differences are obtained for both massive particles and light signals. The radial motion's impact on the Schwarzschild time delay is evaluated, and the results are applied to typical black holes to assess detectability.

Result: The study identifies that the radial motion of the black hole lens affects the leading-order Schwarzschild time delay. When the lens moves towards the observer, the flight time of ultrarelativistic massive particles decreases, while moving away increases it. The paper also calculates the magnitude of this effect and explores its potential detection in astronomical scenarios.

Conclusion: This paper advances our understanding of gravitational time delays in dynamic spacetimes, offering new insights into testing general relativity. The findings are valuable for high-energy physics, cosmology, and future observational strategies involving relativistic particles and black holes.

Abstract: The leading-order gravitational time delay of relativistic neutral massive
particles (e.g., neutrinos or high-energy cosmic-ray particles) caused by a
moving Schwarzschild black hole with a constant radial velocity is investigated
for the first time. On the basis of the equations of motion in the spacetime of
the moving lens, we achieve a new unified formula for the travel times of
relativistic massive and massless particles propagating from the source to the
observer within the first post-Minkowskian approximation. The analytical form
of the difference between the travel times of a relativistic massive particle
and a light signal in this geometry, as well as that of two relativistic
massive particles, is thus obtained in the weak-field and slow-motion limit.
The influence of the radial lens motion on the leading-order Schwarzschild time
delay of relativistic massive particles is then discussed. It is found that in
the slow-motion limit, the radial lens motion towards the observer decreases
the flight time of an ultrarelativistic massive particle, when compared with
the case of no translational motion of the central body. Conversely, if the
lens gets away from the detector radially under the same conditions, the
propagation process of the particle will slow down and its flight time will
thus increase in comparison with the Schwarzschild case. Finally, we analyze
the magnitude of the full radial motion effect of the lens and evaluate the
possibility of its astronomical detection by modeling three typical black holes
as the lens respectively.

</details>

### [80] [On Geometrization of Classical Fields II (MES: dark matter, energy)](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14313)
*V. I. Noskov*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: 研究继续探讨4维Finsler空间中的类 substance在MES模型中的几何化，涉及引力和电磁相互作用的非线性几何关系，暗物质和能量的估算，以及场相互作用的对称性。

  <summary>Details</summary>

Abstract: The study of arXiv:2502.01174 geometrization of classical fields in the
4d--Finsler space of MES (Model of Embedded Spaces) is continued. The model
postulates a proper metric set of a distributed matter element and states that

Embedding geometry is a Finsler-like relativistic geometry with connectivity
depending on the mechanical state of matter: torsion and non-metricity are
absent. The Least Action Principle provides the geodesic motion of matter,
leads to nonlinearity of the system of field equations, anisotropy and
Weyl-invariance of gravitation MES. It is shown that in the special case of
Embedding (conformal Weyl metric) the geometrization of fields can be realized
completely: namely, to obtain Maxwell-type equations and to find the
gravitational sources, lying behind the $\Lambda$ term of Einstein-type
equation. They are identified as dark matter and energy of the Universe, and
the estimates of their material-field composition are close to the observed
ones. It is also shown that the Embedding's gravitational and electromagnetic
potentials are mutual gauge fields. Further development of the MES implies
going beyond the Weyl metric.

### [83] [Clarifying the relation between covariantly conserved currents and Noether's theorem](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14454)
*Nuno Barros e Sá,Miguel A. S. Pinto*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: The paper explores the conditions under which Noether's second theorem can be used to derive covariantly conserved currents from local symmetries, comparing global and local symmetries.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Understanding the relationship between global and local symmetries and their conserved currents is fundamental in theoretical physics, particularly in gauge theories and general relativity.

Method: The authors use the tools of calculus, following Noether's original approach, avoiding advanced mathematical frameworks to make the content accessible.

Result: The paper establishes when Noether's second theorem applies to covariant conservation, offering a clearer link between global and local symmetries and their conserved currents.

Conclusion: This analysis provides a more accessible explanation of Noether's theorems, highlighting the conditions for deriving covariant conserved currents from local symmetries.

Abstract: On one hand, proper conservation laws, that is, the existence of local
functions of the fields whose divergence vanishes on-shell, are associated with
global symmetries and are a consequence of Noether's first theorem. On the
other hand, covariant conservation laws, i.e., the same type of laws but
featuring a covariant divergence, are associated with local symmetries and are
a consequence (under certain conditions) of Noether's second theorem. In this
paper, we clarify under which conditions Noether's second theorem, which is
mostly known for providing relations between the equations of motion of a
theory that possesses some local symmetries, can be used to generate
covariantly conservation laws. We also investigate the relation between the
conserved current of a theory with global symmetry and the covariantly
conserved current of the corresponding local symmetry. We treat these issues
using only the tools of Calculus, in the fashion of Noether's original article,
avoiding the somewhat complicated mathematical tools that plague much of the
literature on this topic, thus making the article readable for the general
physicist.

</details>

### [85] [Complete quasinormal modes of Type-D black holes](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14635)
*Changkai Chen,Jiliang Jing,Zhoujian Cao,Mengjie Wang*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: 研究发现了黑洞量子正常模式（QNMs）的两个主要问题，并提出了一种新方法来解决它们，展示了计算精确度高达10^-10的结果。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: QNMs是理解黑洞量子力学和引力波的重要工具，解决它们的困难性与计算效率对理论物理和天文学有重要意义。

Method: 研究者开发了一种通过解析连续方法消除连接参数依赖的Heun函数方法，解决了QNMs跨越或位于负虚轴的问题，大幅提高了计算效率。

Result: 通过精确计算提供了解决两个开放问题的方法 validate的QNMs，结果 Error小于1e-10。

Conclusion: 这种方法不仅解释了QNMs的不连续性，还展示了高ℓ不寻常模式的行为，显著超越了现有方法。

Abstract: Quasinormal mode (QNM) spectra of black holes exhibit two open problems
[Conf. Proc. C 0405132, 145 (2004); CQG 26, 163001 (2009)]: (i) the
discontinuity in highly damped QNMs between Schwarzschild and Kerr solutions as
$a \to 0$, and (ii) the unexplained spectral proximity between QNMs and
algebraically special (AS) frequencies, particularly the anomalous multiplet
splitting for Kerr $\ell=2$, $m \geq 0$ modes. We develop a novel method to
compute complete QNM spectra for Type-D black holes, solving both problems and
establishing a mathematical framework for boundary value problems of
dissipative systems. Using analytic continuation of radial eigenvalue
equations, our method eliminates the dependence on auxiliary parameters in the
connection formulas for confluent Heun solutions. This breakthrough overcomes
the long-standing challenge of calculating QNMs that cross or lie on the
negative imaginary axis (NIA).For Schwarzschild and Kerr spacetimes ($0 \leq n
\leq 41$, $2 \leq \ell \leq 16$), we present complete spectra validated through
scattering amplitudes with errors $<10^{-10}$.The results provide definitive
solutions to both open problems: (i) The inability of conventional methods to
compute QNMs crossing or residing on the NIA leads to apparent discontinuities
in Kerr spectra as $a \to 0$. (ii) When a QNM exactly coincides with the AS
frequency, an additional QNM (unconventional mode) appears nearby.For the Kerr
case with $\ell=2$, overtone sequences from both unconventional and AS modes
exhibit precisely $2\ell+1$ branches, without multiplets or supersymmetry
breaking at AS frequencies.Our method confirms Leung's conjecture of
high-$\ell$ unconventional mode deviations from the NIA through the first
$\ell=3$ calculation.Moreover, this paradigm surpasses the state-of-the-art
Cook's continued fraction and isomonodromic methods in computational
efficiency.

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: Combines multi-scale multi-headed autoencoder with Bayesian inference (Markov Chain Monte Carlo) for signal separation and parameter estimation.

Abstract: Extracting the faint gravitational-wave background (GWB) signal from dominant

components remain significant challenges for traditional methods like
cross-correlation analysis. We propose a novel hybrid approach that combines

multi-scale multi-headed autoencoder (MSMHAutoencoder) architecture to separate

### [91] [Progress toward the detection of the gravitational-wave background from stellar-mass binary black holes: a mock data challenge](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14179)
*Xiao-Xiao Kou,Muhammed Saleem,Vuk Mandic,Colm Talbot,Eric Thrane*

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: The paper outlines a coherent detection method using realistic data, comparing it to the cross-correlation approach. They involve phase evolution modeling for binary black holes to enhance sensitivity, which requires more detailed systematic error analysis.

Result: The coherent detection method shows promise by improving sensitivity, allowing for more precise detection of the background, though at a computational cost.

Conclusion: By implementing this coherent method with realistic data, the paper paves the way for more sensitive gravitational wave searches, enhancing our ability to detect and understand cosmic events but requiring significant advancements in computational resources and error understanding.

Abstract: While the third LIGO--Virgo gravitational-wave transient catalog includes 90
signals, it is believed that ${\cal O}(10^5)$ binary black holes merge
somewhere in the Universe every year. Although these signals are too weak to be
detected individually with current observatories, they combine to create a
stochastic background, which is potentially detectable in the near future.
LIGO--Virgo searches for the gravitational-wave background using
cross-correlation have so far yielded upper limits. However, Smith \& Thrane
(2017) showed that a vastly more sensitive ``coherent'' search can be carried
out by incorporating information about the phase evolution of binary black hole
signals. This improved sensitivity comes at a cost; the coherent method is
computationally expensive and requires a far more detailed understanding of
systematic errors than is required for the cross-correlation search. In this
work, we demonstrate the coherent approach with realistic data, paving the way
for a gravitational-wave background search with unprecedented sensitivity.

Abstract: We investigate tachyon production in noncommutative de Sitter space by

Abstract: A primary goal of string phenomenology is to identify realistic
four-dimensional physics within the landscape of string theory solutions. In

  <summary>Details</summary>

Result: 确定了超对称标准模型的真空几何结构，包含三个不可约部分，分别为不同维度的有理簇，能够通过gauge不变算子描述。

typically a continuous manifold, called the vacuum moduli space, parametrized

preserving superpotential at renormalizable order, we use Gr\"obner bases to

Gr\"obner bases have doubly exponential computational complexity (for this
case, $7^{2^{1023}}$ operations); we exploit symmetry and multigrading to
render the computation tractable. This geometry has three irreducible
components of complex dimensions $1$, $15$, and $29$, each being a so-called
rational variety. The defining equations of the components express the
solutions to F-terms and D-terms in terms of the gauge invariant operators and
are interpreted in terms of classical geometric constructions.

</details>

### [96] [The Vacuum Moduli Space of the Minimal Supersymmetric Standard Model](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13868)
*Yang-Hui He,Vishnu Jejjala,Brent D. Nelson,Hal Schenck,Michael Stillman*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: A TCK paper detailing the detailed algebraic geometry of the vacuum moduli space in the MSSM setup. They divide into three main components, study their dimensions and rationality, and rederive known results for the electroweak sector.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: This paper is a follow-up to arXiv:1111.5832, expanding on the vacuum moduli space study in MSSM and using symplectic quotients to analyze algebraic structures.

Method: Algebraic geometry, specifically studying symplectic quotients, decomposition of varieties, and computation of dimensions and rationality.

Result: The variety splits into three components with specified dimensions, and images under the quotient map are shown to be rational. These results align with known electroweak sector findings and use incidence varieties for geometric description.

Conclusion: The paper concludes that components of the MSSM's vacuum moduli space exhibit predictable structure, with three main irreducible components whose properties are thoroughly analyzed, providing a deeper understanding of MSSM's algebraic structure.

Abstract: A starting point in the study of the minimal supersymmetric Standard Model
(MSSM) is the vacuum moduli space, which is a highly complicated algebraic
variety: it is the image of an affine variety $X \subset \mathbb{C}^{49}$ under
a symplectic quotient map $\phi$ to $\mathbb{C}^{973}$. Previous work computed
the vacuum moduli space of the electroweak sector; geometrically this
corresponds to studying a restriction of $\phi$: $\mathbb{C}^{13}
\stackrel{\phi^{\texttt{res}}}{\longrightarrow} \mathbb{C}^{22}$. We analyze
the geometry of the full vacuum moduli space for superpotentials $W_{\rm
minimal}$ (without neutrinos) and $W_{\rm MSSM}$ (with neutrinos) in
$\mathbb{C}^{973}$. In both cases, we prove that $X$ consists of three
irreducible components $X_1$, $X_2$, and $X_3$, and determine the images $M_i$
of the $X_i$ under $\phi$. For $W_{\rm minimal}$ we show they have,
respectively, dimensions $1$, $15$, and $29$, and prove that each of the $M_i$
is a rational variety, while for $W_{\rm MSSM}$ we show that $M_3$ is the only
component. Restricting the $M_i$ to the electroweak sector, we recover known
results. We describe the components of the vacuum moduli space geometrically in
terms of incidence varieties to a product of Segre varieties.

</details>

*Ashoke Sen*

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究不同超对称弦理论中模空间的行为及其物理意义，试图理解理论上能否通过有限时间实验确定模值，这可能涉及弦论的模空间和几何结构情况。

Method: 分析了多维平滑空间中的极值行为，考虑了镜像对称性和共形转换，通过构造经典解来举例模空间的转换情况。利用共形场论和弦论知识来推导结论。

Abstract: N=2, 4 and 8 supersymmetric string theories in four dimensional flat
space-time have moduli space of vacua. We argue that starting from a theory
where the moduli approach a particular moduli space point A at infinity, we can
construct a classical solution that contains an arbitrarily large space-time
region where the moduli take values corresponding to any other moduli space
point B of our choice to any desired accuracy. Therefore the observables of a
theory with a given set of asymptotic values of the moduli will have complete
information on the observables for any other asymptotic values of the moduli.
Also it is physically impossible for any experiment, performed over a finite
time, to determine the asymptotic values of the moduli. We point out the
difference between asymptotically flat space-time and asymptotically AdS
space-time in this regard and discuss the possible implication of these results
for holographic duals of string theories in flat space-time. For N=2
supersymmetric theories, A and B could correspond to compactifications on
topologically distinct Calabi-Yau manifolds related by flop or conifold
transitions.

### [98] [Probing Non-Graviton Spectra in $\mathcal{N}=4$ SYM via BMN truncation and S-Duality](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13887)
*Abhijit Gadde,Eunwoo Lee,Rajat Raj,Shivansh Tomar*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper investigates the one-loop cohomology of N=4 SYM, focusing on BMN truncations and BMN indices for SU(N) SYM, revealing a bosonic Fock space structure incompatible with non-interacting gravitons. It also examines S-dual pairs where BMN indices mismatch, suggesting new cohomology subrings compatible with S-duality.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Understanding the cohomological structures and their implications in N=4 SYM, particularly the BMN truncation, is crucial for testing the AdS/CFT correspondence and uncovering new physics within the theory.

Method: Systematic algorithm using residues to compute BMN indices for SU(N) SYM, with N=2,...,6. Analyzes S-dual pairs and identifies discrepancies in BMN-sector indices, linking it to new cohomology subrings compatible with S-duality.

Result: Expressed BMN indices as rational functions with denominator terms indicating bosonic generators, with a Fock space structure not explained by non-interacting gravitons. Discrepancies in BMN indices for S-dual pairs suggest new cohomology subrings that match under S-duality with letter-based truncations.

Conclusion: The findings challenge existing understanding of the BMN sector and hint at a novel microstructure within supersymmetric black holes, potentially involving new cohomology subrings that maintain S-duality compatibility.

Abstract: The one-loop cohomology of N=4 SYM is conjectured to be isomorphic to the
exact cohomology. As a result, its truncations are expected to be subrings of
the exact cohomology. We study the superconformal index restricted over one
such truncation known as the BMN truncation. We present a systematic algorithm
to compute the BMN index using the method of residues. We compute the BMN index
for SU(N) SYM for N = 2,...,6 in closed form. It is expressed as a rational
function of the fugacity. A term of the type (1-x) in the denominator indicates
the presence of a bosonic generator counted with fugacity x. We find a rich and
universal set of such terms in the denominator showing an interesting bosonic
Fock space in the spectrum of protected operators. This Fock space cannot be
explained as coming from the non-interacting supersymmetric graviton gas far
away from the black hole as in the grey-galaxy solutions because the charges of
the bosonic generators are not compatible with those of the supersymmetric
gravitons. This suggests a novel microstructure within the supersymmetric black
hole itself. We also examine the indices of S-dual pairs SO(2N+1) and Sp(N)
SYM. Although their full 1/16-BPS indices coincide, we find discrepancies in
their BMN-sector indices. As the BMN indices restricted to the graviton sector
are expected to be the same, this mismatch allows us to identify non-graviton
cohomologies. We explicitly find one of them in the SO(7) theory that is
responsible for the mismatch of the BMN index. We also show that indices
restricted to other one-loop cohomology truncations, in general, do not match
under S-duality. If the conjecture of exactness of one-loop cohomology is
correct, this suggests the presence of new cohomology subrings that match under
S-duality with the letter-based truncations of the one-loop cohomology. This
offers a way to check the one-loop exactness conjecture.

</details>

*Jefferson Monção da Silva,João Paulo M. Pitelli*

function of an Unruh-deWitt detector coupled to a massless scalar field. In

with no conical deficit and (due to the rapid switching on and off) is
classically isolated from the conical region. The scalar field was supposed to
be continuous at the three dimensional timelike hypersurface connecting both

were only due to the deficit angle of the outer conical region. In this paper,
we study the response function of the Unruh-deWitt detector on the same
classical framework, but exploring the effects of the choice of boundary

detector, which effectively ``feels'' the combined effect of conicity +
boundary condition.

Abstract: In this paper, we propose a revision to the Quantum Extremal Surface (QES)
prescription, which plays a crucial role in describing the entanglement entropy
of black holes. While derivations exist for the original QES prescription using
the replica trick, they rely on a saddle point approximation that faces
challenges when the number of replicas approaches unity. We highlight these
challenges and derive a refined formula for the entanglement entropy that
incorporates a weighted summation over multiple surfaces, contrasting the QES
prescription's reliance on a single extremal surface. We validate our
formulation by demonstrating consistency with expected results for both the
early and late stages of black hole evaporation, confirming its alignment with
the unitary evolution depicted by the Page curve.

Abstract: In this paper we investigate 5-point Liouville conformal block with a level 2
degenerate field insertion. Our main tool is the BPZ differential equation,
which, upon placing three of the insertions at the standard positions $\infty$,
$1$, and $0$, reduces to a linear differential equation which is of order two
in the degenerate insertion point $z$, and order one in the remaining point
$x$. In a previous paper, it was conjectured that the solution could be
expressed in terms of a single hypergeometric function and its derivative, with
coefficients computable via recursive relations up to the desired order $x^k$.
In this paper, we simplify these recursion relations and provide a rigorous
inductive proof of the conjecture.
  Our representation of the 5-point conformal block readily facilitates the
connection between various analyticity regions through classical connection
formulae for the hypergeometric function.
  In the quasi-classical limit, the 5-point BPZ equation reduces to the Heun
equation. Consequently, we recover a recently proposed representation of the
Heun equation in terms of a single hypergeometric function, which has proven to
be highly effective in the analysis of gravitational perturbation of black
holes.

Abstract: We investigate the gravitational scattering of a spinning probe mass in a
Kerr background using the worldline quantum field theory (WQFT) approach. This
corresponds to the leading term (0SF) in the gravitational self-force expansion

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 分析环代数的结构有助于理解理论的基础对称和对偶性，这在共形场论和弦理论中非常重要。</motivation>

Method: 通过研究操作积展开的结合性约束，推导出环代数的性质和结构特征。这包括对约束条件的系统性分析和对可能的代数结构进行分类的可能性排除，以确认唯一性。</method>

Result: 结果显示该代数由中心荷唯一确定，没有额外的自由参数。同时，OPE系数的模式表明该代数不能由对称共轭轨产生。</result>

Conclusion: 论文得出4D $ar{N}=4$ SU$(N)$理论的环代数由中心荷唯一决定，且无法从对称共轭轨构造。这可能提示该理论有独特的代数结构和独特的对称性，需要进一步研究其与其他理论的联系。</conclusion>

Abstract: The chiral algebra of 4D $\mathcal{N}=4$ SU$(N)$ super-Yang-Mills theory is
an $\mathcal{N}=4$ superconformal vertex operator algebra. We analyse the
structure of this algebra by studying recursively the constraints that are
required by the associativity of the operator product expansion. We find that
the algebra is uniquely characterized by the central charge (which can take an
arbitrary value), without any additional free parameter. Furthermore, the
truncation pattern of the OPE coefficients suggests that the algebra cannot
arise from the symmetric orbifold.

</details>


### [107] [Higher loops in AdS: applications to boundary CFT](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14699)
*Simone Giombi,Zimo Sun*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper uses Euclidean AdS space to study BCFT and applies the ε-expansion to analyze the critical O(N) model in 4−ε dimensions. They compute conformal data in BCFT using higher-loop calculations and apply Padé approximants for three-dimensional estimates. The main results include BCFT observables, boundary central charges, and significant findings in universality classes.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses fundamental questions in conformal field theories and their boundary conditions, providing new insights into BCFT observables and central charges.

Method: The authors use a combination of ε-expansion, AdS/CFT correspondence, and Padé approximants to calculate conformal data in BCFT.

Result: They determine the free energy, one-point functions, and boundary central charges in BCFT for the O(N) universality classes.

Conclusion: The study offers valuable tools for calculating observables in BCFT and estimates important central charges, contributing to a better understanding of the underlying physics.

Abstract: The Euclidean Anti-de Sitter (AdS) space provides a natural framework for
studying boundary conformal field theory (BCFT). We analyze the conformal
boundary conditions of the critical O$(N)$ model in $d=4-\epsilon$ dimensions
using the $\epsilon$-expansion, and extract some BCFT observables through
higher-loop calculations in AdS. Specifically, in the so-called "ordinary"
universality class, we determine the free energy to four-loop order and the
one-point function of the lightest O$(N)$ singlet operator to three-loop order.
In the symmetry breaking "normal" universality class, we derive the two-loop
free energy and compute the leading correction to the one-point function of the
lightest O($N$) vector. We apply Pad\'e approximants to extract the
corresponding conformal data in three dimensions. In particular, from a
suitable dimensional continuation of the free energy in AdS, we obtain
estimates for the boundary central charge of the BCFT in $d=3$.

</details>


### [108] [On the scalar tachyons creation in noncommutative de Sitter space-time](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.13775)
*Slimane Zaim*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper explores tachyon production in noncommutative de Sitter space by solving the deformed Klein-Gordon equation, finding that noncommutativity reduces the effective temperature and that the noncommutative parameter plays a role similar to an electric field in standard tachyon production.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper aims to understand how noncommutative geometry affects tachyon production in a de Sitter space, which is a model for an expanding universe. This is important for understanding early universe or high-energy physics scenarios where tachyons and noncommutativity are relevant.

Method: The authors used the Bogoliubov transformation method to solve the deformed Klein-Gordon equation, a mathematical tool that allows for the calculation of particle creation in a time-dependent background. By analyzing the resulting number density of scalar tachyons, they were able to characterize the spectrum of these particles and their thermal distribution.

Result: The key findings are that noncommutativity reduces the effective temperature during tachyon production, consistent with previous studies on particle creation in de Sitter space. Additionally, the noncommutative parameter's role is equivalent to an electric field in standard de Sitter space tachyon production.

Conclusion: The paper provides insights into the interplay between noncommutative geometry and tachyon production, suggesting that noncommutativity can act as a mechanism to modulate the temperature and dynamics of tachyon fields in cosmological settings. This could have implications for models of inflation or cosmic phase transitions.

Abstract: We investigate tachyon production in noncommutative de Sitter space by
solving the deformed Klein-Gordon equation. Using the Bogoliubov transformation
method, we compute the number density of created scalar tachyons and
demonstrate that their spectrum follows a thermal distribution. Our analysis
reveals that noncommutativity reduces the effective temperature of tachyon
production, analogous to its effect on ordinary particle creation. Furthermore,
we establish that the role of the noncommutative parameter in tachyon
production is functionally equivalent to that of an electric field in standard
particle production in de Sitter space.

</details>

*Martin Bies,Miķelis E. Miķelsons,Andrew P. Turner*

TL;DR: The paper presents FTheoryTools, a software module for OSCAR, which automates F-theory model building tasks like G4-fluxes and blowups, using a database for reproducibility. A stress test using a challenging geometry shows its effectiveness for future research in string phenomenology.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: String phenomenology aims to find realistic physics in string theory solutions, which are complex in F-theory. The need for computational tools to handle difficult geometries drives the development of FTheoryTools.

Method: FTheoryTools automates tasks such as G4-flux enumeration and blowups, uses a MaRDI-based database, and applies to a specific geometry to demonstrate its capabilities.

Result: FTheoryTools effectively handles complex F-theory geometries, showing potential for future research. It enhances collaboration and reproducibility through a structured database.

Conclusion: The development of FTheoryTools addresses the computational challenges in F-theory, making string phenomenology more accessible and feasible for future studies. The tool's integration into OSCAR and its database contribution are significant advancements in the field, supporting both collaboration and research.

Abstract: A primary goal of string phenomenology is to identify realistic
four-dimensional physics within the landscape of string theory solutions. In
F-theory, such solutions are encoded in the geometry of singular elliptic
fibrations, whose study often requires particularly challenging and cumbersome
computations. In this work, we introduce FTheoryTools, a novel software module
integrated into the OSCAR computer algebra system, designed to automate the
complex and tedious tasks involved in F-theory model building. Key features of
FTheoryTools include the enumeration of G4-fluxes, the capability to perform
blowups on arbitrary (including non-toric) loci, and a literature database of
existing F-theory constructions employing a MaRDI-based data format for
enhanced collaboration and reproducibility. As a demonstration of its power, we
present a stress test by applying FTheoryTools to the challenging F-theory
geometry with most flux vacua (arXiv:1511.03209). Our results illustrate the
potential of FTheoryTools to streamline F-theory research and pave the way for
future developments in the computational study of string phenomenology.

### [110] [pynamicalsys: A Python toolkit for the analysis of dynamical systems](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14044)
*Matheus Rolim Sales,Leonardo Costa de Souza,Daniel Borin,Michele Mugnaine,José Danilo Szezech Jr.,Ricardo Luiz Viana,Iberê Luiz Caldas,Edson Denis Leonel,Chris G. Antonopoulos*

TL;DR: This paper introduces pynamicalsys, an open-source Python module for analyzing nonlinear dynamical systems, offering various tools like trajectory simulation and Lyapunov exponents, with examples and a Jupyter notebook provided.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper's motivation is to bridge the gap between the theoretical study of nonlinear dynamics and practical computational tools, making it accessible to researchers and educators without extensive coding expertise.

Method: The authors developed a Python module named pynamicalsys, leveraging Python's libraries for numerical computation, visualization, and GUI, with an object-oriented architecture for ease of use. They used Jupyter notebooks for demonstrations and performance benchmarks.

Result: The module successfully implements several analytical tools and demonstrates their effectiveness through reproducible examples, showing its utility in research and teaching.

Conclusion: pynamicalsys provides an accessible and powerful tool for studying nonlinear dynamical systems, enhancing both research and education in this field.

Abstract: Since Lorenz's seminal work on a simplified weather model, the numerical
analysis of nonlinear dynamical systems has become one of the main subjects of
research in physics. Despite of that, there remains a need for accessible,
efficient, and easy-to-use computational tools to study such systems. In this
paper, we introduce pynamicalsys, a simple yet powerful open-source Python
module for the analysis of nonlinear dynamical systems. In particular,
pynamicalsys implements tools for trajectory simulation, bifurcation diagrams,
Lyapunov exponents and several others chaotic indicators, period orbit
detection and their manifolds, as well as escape and basins analysis. It also
includes many built-in models and the use of custom models is straighforward.
We demonstrate the capabilities of pynamicalsys through a series of examples
that reproduces well-known results in the literature while developing the
mathematical analysis at the same time. We also provide the Jupyter notebook
containing all the code used in this paper, including performance benchmarks.
pynamicalsys is freely available via the Python Package Index (PyPI) and is
indented to support both research and teaching in nonlinear dynamics.

</details>

### [112] [Stochastic motility energetics reveals cooperative bacterial swarming in optical tweezers](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14573)
*Clara Luque-Rioja,Horacio López-Menéndez,Macarena Calero,Niccoló Caselli,Diego Herráez-Aguilar,Juan P. G. Villaluenga,Francisco Monroy*

Main category: physics.bio-ph

TL;DR: 研究通过结合光聚力测力仪和多粒子追踪，在随机热力学框架下，观察了Proteus mirabilis菌落的单菌群动力学行为。结果显示，菌落的旋转运动超出被动摩擦极限，并且表现出非平衡的流动。使用活跃的布朗运动模型化菌落轨迹，计算出在合作耦合与热涨落作用下，菌落动力学表现出消耗率较高的流动状态。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 微生物群落中的协作行为，尤其是 flagellar 与否的共同移动，了解这些行为对生命科学很重要。这项研究试图量化单菌群的动态，尤其是在有限空间中的能量消耗情况。

Method: 研究使用了光聚力测力仪和多粒子追踪，结合随机热力学方法，分析了Proteus mirabilis菌落的动力学行为。

Result: 结果显示了游动菌落的非平衡流动特征， flagellar 运动的影响超出被动摩擦的限制，表现出非平衡的流动。同时，通过活跃的布朗运动模型化，计算得到了较高的流动消耗率。

Conclusion: 这项研究为理解微粒涉嫌的物理原理和微生物协作提供了新的见解。该方法可以推广到其他微粒系统，如主动颗粒或生物系统，研究群体动力学的协作行为。

Abstract: Bacterial flagellar swarming enables dense microbial populations to migrate
collectively across surfaces, often resulting in emergent, coordinated
behaviors. However, probing the underlying energetics of swarming at the single
cluster level remains a challenge. Here, we combine optical tweezers and
multiparticle tracking within a stochastic thermodynamic framework to
characterize the active motility of confined Proteus mirabilis clusters. Using
the Photon Momentum Method to directly measure trapping forces, we show that
swarming clusters generate persistent, dissipative flows indicative of non
equilibrium stationary motility within confined solenoidal mesostructures.
These flagellar rotational dynamics break detailed balance in mesoscopic force
space and exceed the limits of passive friction, as evidenced by force velocity
correlations and vortex like circulations. By coarse graining cluster
trajectories into an active Brownian phase space, we quantify the work
performed by bacterial swarms at cooperative coupling to thermal fluctuations,
resulting in dissipative Ohmic like currents overcoming conservative trapping.
Our findings establish a generalizable approach to quantify collective motility
and energetic dissipation in active bacterial clusters, offering new insights
into the physical principles governing microbial cooperativity.

</details>


### [113] [Active viscoelastic condensates provide controllable mechanical anchor points](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14591)
*Oliver W. Paulin,Júlia Garcia-Baucells,Luise Zieger,Sebastian Aland,Alexander Dammermann,David Zwicker*

Main category: physics.bio-ph

TL;DR: 该论文探讨了生物材料如何在快速自组装和机械强度之间取得平衡。通过模型和实验，发现粘弹性材料在结构稳定性与动力学行为之间起到关键作用。利用这些发现，结论为其他系统如附着锚定提供了指导性原则。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 生物材料在早期胚胎中的附着锚定功能需要在快速组装和机械强度之间平衡，这在生物力学中具有重要意义。文章通过模型和实验，探讨阻尼或材料特性如何影响这种平衡，给我们提供了设计其他类似结构的指导。

Method: 作者构建了粘弹性增长模型，分析了不同材料incorporation方案对生长动力学和机械强度的影响。通过理论推导和实验证实了模型的适用性。

Result: 模型结果验证了阻尼可以限制聚合物的生长，但提供结构稳定性。通过调节材料的材料参数，可以在 agile 生长和强健的机械性能之间找到平衡。

Conclusion: 该研究为需要快速聚集和机械强度的生物材料设计提供了原则性指导，例如附着锚定等结构。结果不仅给出了理论分析，还与实验证据吻合，验证了模型的适用性。

Abstract: Many biological materials must couple mechanical strength with the ability to
rapidly self-assemble at a specific location. In particular, biomolecular
condensates readily self-assemble via phase separation, but may also need to
resist external forces to fulfil their function. Spatial localisation of
condensate formation can be controlled by active cores that preferentially
drive the production of condensate material at a particular point, while
resistance to external forces can be facilitated by viscoelastic material
properties. To investigate the interplay of these two processes, we develop a
continuum model of viscoelastic growth around an active core. We find that
viscoelastic stresses restrict condensate growth, but also impart resistance to
deformation. We investigate the effect of different incorporation schemes on
growth dynamics, and test the influence of mechanical properties on condensate
strength. Finally, we compare the predictions of our model to experimental data
from centrosomes in C. elegans embryos, identifying a parameter regime in which
rapid growth can be combined with appropriate mechanical strength, and studying
how strain-dependent material incorporation may lead to isotropic growth of
scaffold material. Our results provide general design principles for other
materials that must reconcile rapid, localised self-assembly with mechanical
strength, such as focal adhesions.

</details>

### [116] [Accurate Chemistry Collection: Coupled cluster atomization energies for broad chemical space](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14492)
*Sebastian Ehlert,Jan Hermann,Thijs Vogels,Victor Garcia Satorras,Stephanie Lanius,Marwin Segler,Derk P. Kooi,Kenji Takeda,Chin-Wei Huang,Giulia Luise,Rianne van den Berg,Paola Gori-Giorgi,Amir Karton*

Main category: physics.chem-ph

TL;DR: The paper introduces a new dataset for thermochemical properties that addresses the limitations of existing datasets by covering a broad chemical space.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The authors highlight the need for large, diverse datasets to improve computational chemistry methods, especially for challenging properties like heats of formation and TAEs.

Method: They created a dataset of 76,879 TAEs using CCSD(T)/CBS with a novel enumeration and sampling method to cover elements up to argon.

Result: The dataset provides high accuracy and broad coverage, enabling more reliable data-driven chemistry methods.

Conclusion: Exemplifying this dataset is crucial for advancing computational chemistry with precise and diverse data.

Abstract: Accurate thermochemical data with sub-chemical accuracy (i.e., within $\pm$1
kcal mol$^{-1}$ from sufficiently accurate experimental or theoretical
reference data) is essential for the development and improvement of
computational chemistry methods. Challenging thermochemical properties such as
heats of formation and total atomization energies (TAEs) are of particular
interest because they rigorously test the ability of computational chemistry
methods to accurately describe complex chemical transformations involving
multiple bond rearrangements. Yet, existing thermochemical datasets that
confidently reach this level of accuracy are limited in either size or scope.
Datasets with highly accurate reference values include a small number of data
points, and larger datasets provide less accurate data or only cover a narrow
portion of the chemical space. The existing datasets are therefore insufficient
for developing data-driven methods with predictive accuracy over a large
chemical space. The Microsoft Research Accurate Chemistry Collection (MSR-ACC)
will address this challenge. Here, it offers the MSR-ACC/TAE25 dataset of
76,879 total atomization energies obtained at the CCSD(T)/CBS level via the
W1-F12 thermochemical protocol. The dataset is constructed to exhaustively
cover chemical space for all elements up to argon by enumerating and sampling
chemical graphs, thus avoiding bias towards any particular subspace of the
chemical space (such as drug-like, organic, or experimentally observed
molecules). With this first dataset in MSR-ACC, we enable data-driven
approaches for developing predictive computational chemistry methods with
unprecedented accuracy and scope.

</details>

*Henry Thompson,Matteo Bonanomi,Jacob Pedersen,Oksana Plekan,Nitish Pal,Cesare Grazioli,Kevin C. Prince,Bruno N. C. Tenorio,Michele Devetta,Davide Faccialà,Caterina Vozzi,Paolo Piseri,Miltcho B. Holland,Felix Allum,Daniel Rolles,Piero Decleva,Michael S. Schuurman,Ruharid J. G. Forbes,Sonia Coriani,Carlo Callegari,Russell S. Minns,Michele Di Fraia*

Main category: physics.chem-ph

TL;DR: The paper introduces a novel method using X-ray pulses to study both valence and core electronic states in photochemical reactions, providing detailed insights into the dynamics of CS₂ molecules when excited. The technique successfully differentiates contributions from singlet and triplet excited states, clarifying aspects of internal conversion and intersystem crossing. This approach bridges the gap between experimental and computational methods, enhancing our understanding of ultrafast molecular transformations.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses the challenge of studying ultrafast electronic and structural changes in molecules during photochemical transformations, which is a difficult task due to the need for precise experimental and computational techniques. This research often involves comparing different approaches, such as measuring valence and core electronic states separately, which may be time-consuming and less effective. By introducing a method that combines high-resolution X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) with advanced FEL-based techniques, the paper provides a more integrated and efficient approach to understanding these transformations. The study of CS₂ during photoexcitation is particularly interesting as it involves controversial mechanisms like internal conversion and intersystem crossing, which are critical for understanding the pre-dissociation dynamics. The paper's contribution is in demonstrating how this new experimental technique can complement existing computational methods, leading to clearer and more precise conclusions about the spin-selectivity and dynamics of these processes.

Method: The research outlines the method used, which involves using X-ray pulses from a seeded free-electron laser (FEL) to generate high-resolution, time-resolved X-ray photoelectron spectra (XPS). These spectra specifically capture weak satellite states arising from shake-down processes in a valence-excited molecule. This approach allows for the simultaneous investigation of both valence and core electronic states, which traditionally required separate methods. The FEL-based XPS system enables the measurement of XPS spectra efficiently, combining the strengths of valence and core state research. For the application, the method was applied to photoexcited CS₂ molecules, where the dynamics involve internal conversion (IC) and intersystem crossing (ISC), which are competing processes in determining the pre-dissociation pathway. The researchers used XPS spectra obtained at the FERMI FEL and compared high-resolution measurements to computational results from multireference quantum chemical calculations to highlight the sensitivity of shake-down satellite channels to electronic and geometric changes. Additionally, they developed a propensity rule based on spin-selectivity observed in the shake-down processes, which allowed them to accurately assign contributions from singlet and triplet excited states along the pre-dissociation pathway.

Result: The experimental results demonstrate that high-resolution XPS spectra at FERMI reveal significant contributions from shake-down satellite channels, which are highly sensitive to changes in both valence electronic and geometric structures of the excited CS₂ molecules. These findings resolve uncertainties in assigning the pre-dissociation dynamics, which traditionally involved confusing singlet and triplet state populations. By observing the spin-selectivity of the shake-down process, the researchers were able to unambiguously attribute observed spectral features to specific excited states, thereby clarifying the branching pathways and dynamics involved. This integration of experimental data with computational modeling provides a clearer understanding of the spin-polarized pathways and the role of electronic transitions in the photoexcitation of CS₂ molecules.

Conclusion: The study introduces an innovative approach using X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) with a seeded free-electron laser (FEL) to study the electronic and structural changes in photoexcited molecules. This method effectively combines the benefits of valence and core state investigation, offering high-resolution data to discern spin-selectivity and branching in photochemical reactions. By applying this technique to CS₂, the paper reveals detailed information about the dynamics of photoexcited states, including the contributions of singlet and triplet states, and the interplay of internal conversion and intersystem crossing. The results not only enhance our understanding of specific molecular processes but also pave the way for future developments in ultrafast spectroscopy, bridge the gap between experimental techniques and theoretical modeling, and advance the field of photochemistry by providing a powerful tool to study ultrafast electronic dynamics in molecules.

Abstract: Tracking the multifarious ultrafast electronic and structural changes
occurring in a molecule during a photochemical transformation is a challenging
endeavor that benefits from recent experimental and computational progress in
time-resolved techniques. Measurements of valence electronic states, which
provide a global picture of the bonding structure of the molecule, and core
electronic states, which provide insight into the local environment,
traditionally require different approaches and are often studied separately.
Here, we demonstrate that X-ray pulses from a seeded free-electron laser (FEL)
enable the measurement of high-resolution, time-resolved X-ray photoelectron
spectra (XPS) that capture weak satellite states resulting from shake-down
processes in a valence-excited molecule. This approach effectively combines the
advantages of both valence- and core-state investigations. We applied this
method to investigate photoexcited CS$_2$ molecules, where the role of internal
conversion (IC) and intersystem crossing (ISC) in determining the
pre-dissociation dynamics is controversial. We present XPS spectra from
photoexcited CS$_2$, obtained at the FERMI FEL. High-resolution measurements,
compared to the corresponding spectra obtained from accurate multireference
quantum chemical calculations, reveal that shake-down satellite channels are
highly sensitive to both valence electronic and geometric changes. Previous
studies of the pre-dissociation dynamics have led to uncertain assignments
around the branching between singlet and triplet excited states. We derived a
propensity rule that demonstrates the spin-selectivity of the shake-downs. This
selectivity allows us to unequivocally assign contributions from the bright and
dark singlet excited states with populations tracked along the pre-dissociation
dynamic pathway.

### [118] [Accurate and scalable exchange-correlation with deep learning](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14665)
*Giulia Luise,Chin-Wei Huang,Thijs Vogels,Derk P. Kooi,Sebastian Ehlert,Stephanie Lanius,Klaas J. H. Giesbertz,Amir Karton,Deniz Gunceler,Megan Stanley,Wessel P. Bruinsma,Lin Huang,Xinran Wei,José Garrido Torres,Abylay Katbashev,Bálint Máté,Sékou-Oumar Kaba,Roberto Sordillo,Yingrong Chen,David B. Williams-Young,Christopher M. Bishop,Jan Hermann,Rianne van den Berg,Paola Gori-Giorgi*

Main category: physics.chem-ph

TL;DR: The paper introduces Skala, a deep learning-based XC functional that combines chemical accuracy with computational efficiency for molecular simulations.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The search for accurate and efficient exchange-correlation functionals is crucial for Density Functional Theory (DFT) applications, particularly in predicting molecular and material properties with high precision. The limitations of current XC functionals drive the need for novel approaches that balance accuracy and computational feasibility.

Method: The study employs a deep learning model trained on a large dataset of high-accuracy wavefunction-based calculations. Skala learns representations of the XC functional directly from the data, avoiding traditional handcrafted features while maintaining computational efficiency similar to semi-local DFT methods.

Result: Skala achieves chemical accuracy for atomization energies, scales efficiently, and shows consistent improvement with more data. It also matches hybrid functionals' accuracy with a modest dataset requirement.

Conclusion: This work represents a significant step forward by demonstrating that deep learning can enhance DFT's capabilities, suggesting broader applications in materials and chemical simulations.

Abstract: Density Functional Theory (DFT) is the most widely used electronic structure
method for predicting the properties of molecules and materials. Although DFT
is, in principle, an exact reformulation of the Schr\"odinger equation,
practical applications rely on approximations to the unknown
exchange-correlation (XC) functional. Most existing XC functionals are
constructed using a limited set of increasingly complex, hand-crafted features
that improve accuracy at the expense of computational efficiency. Yet, no
current approximation achieves the accuracy and generality for predictive
modeling of laboratory experiments at chemical accuracy -- typically defined as
errors below 1 kcal/mol. In this work, we present Skala, a modern deep
learning-based XC functional that bypasses expensive hand-designed features by
learning representations directly from data. Skala achieves chemical accuracy
for atomization energies of small molecules while retaining the computational
efficiency typical of semi-local DFT. This performance is enabled by training
on an unprecedented volume of high-accuracy reference data generated using
computationally intensive wavefunction-based methods. Notably, Skala
systematically improves with additional training data covering diverse
chemistry. By incorporating a modest amount of additional high-accuracy data
tailored to chemistry beyond atomization energies, Skala achieves accuracy
competitive with the best-performing hybrid functionals across general main
group chemistry, at the cost of semi-local DFT. As the training dataset
continues to expand, Skala is poised to further enhance the predictive power of
first-principles simulations.

</details>


### [119] [About explosive delayed desorption from methane-doped argon matrices](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14726)
*M. A. Bludov,I. V. Khyzhniy,S. A. Uyutnov,E. V. Savchenko*

Main category: physics.chem-ph

TL;DR: 研究了甲烷在惰性气体矩阵受电子束辐照后的延迟解吸现象，发现高甲烷浓度下出现多次解吸，H原子与粒子爆炸存在相关性，并根据能量传递过程解释了这种现象。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 研究CH4解吸过程，探讨能量传输对实验现象的影响。

Method: 使用射线辐照和压力监测分析解吸特性和结构。通过发光光谱检测放射性产物，并分析压强变化来跟踪解吸过程。利用浓度依赖性分析解吸峰，推断CH4聚集体形成。通过能量传递和捕获过程分析H原子与粒子爆炸的关系。测量在不同浓度下的粒子释放量。研究解吸闪变的能量变化和时间为特征。

Result: 高浓度时出现多次解吸，首次记录了CH4的解吸，发现H原子与粒子爆炸有相关性，解释了能量传递和捕获。粒子释放量线性增加，讨论了闪变强度和间隔变化。

Conclusion: 研究成果揭示了甲烷在惰性矩阵中的解吸动态行为和能量传输机制。揭示了高浓度下多次解吸的现象。H原子与粒子爆炸的在现象间的关系有意义，线性关系和集中现象提供新的研究方向。需进一步研究能量结构和H-H分子结构影响。

Abstract: The features of delayed desorption from CH4-doped Ar matrices irradiated with
an electron beam of subthreshold energy were studied. Radiolysis products were
detected by emission spectroscopy. The total desorption yield was monitored by
recording the pressure in the experimental chamber. Based on the analysis of
the concentration dependence of delayed desorption bursts and their structure,
an assumption was made about the formation of CH4 clusters in Ar matrices. At a
high dopant concentration of 10%, up to three consecutive bursts were recorded.
Delayed desorption from a sample doped with 0.1% CH4 was registered for the
first time. A correlation has been found between the burst of particles and the
flash of luminescence of H atoms. This seemingly contradictory observation of
the correlation of the H atom content with the particle explosion due to their
recombination was explained by analyzing the energy transfer and capture
processes and the features of the energy structure of H2 molecule. A linear
dependence of the total particle yield on the CH4 concentration in the range of
1-10% was found. The dynamics of intensity changes in the sequence of main
flashes and their delay time were discussed.

</details>


### [120] [Accurate Chemistry Collection: Coupled cluster atomization energies for broad chemical space](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14492)
*Sebastian Ehlert,Jan Hermann,Thijs Vogels,Victor Garcia Satorras,Stephanie Lanius,Marwin Segler,Derk P. Kooi,Kenji Takeda,Chin-Wei Huang,Giulia Luise,Rianne van den Berg,Paola Gori-Giorgi,Amir Karton*

Main category: physics.chem-ph

TL;DR: This paper introduces the MSR-ACC/TAE25 dataset with 76,879 total atomization energies, achieving high accuracy by avoiding bias in chemical space and covering elements up to argon.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper addresses the shortage of accurate, large thermochemical datasets by introducing a comprehensive collection of TAEs, enabling better method development in computational chemistry.

Method: Collected TAEs using CCSD(T)/CBS protocol, machine learning enforced geospatial sampling to cover chemical space, excludes complexes with multiple bonds for reduced computational cost.

Result: 76,879 TAEs with chemical space coverage, high accuracy in line with experimental and theoretical standards.

Conclusion: The dataset provides a foundation for accurate and efficient computational chemistry methods in diverse chemical spaces.

Abstract: Accurate thermochemical data with sub-chemical accuracy (i.e., within $\pm$1
kcal mol$^{-1}$ from sufficiently accurate experimental or theoretical
reference data) is essential for the development and improvement of
computational chemistry methods. Challenging thermochemical properties such as
heats of formation and total atomization energies (TAEs) are of particular
interest because they rigorously test the ability of computational chemistry
methods to accurately describe complex chemical transformations involving
multiple bond rearrangements. Yet, existing thermochemical datasets that
confidently reach this level of accuracy are limited in either size or scope.
Datasets with highly accurate reference values include a small number of data
points, and larger datasets provide less accurate data or only cover a narrow
portion of the chemical space. The existing datasets are therefore insufficient
for developing data-driven methods with predictive accuracy over a large
chemical space. The Microsoft Research Accurate Chemistry Collection (MSR-ACC)
will address this challenge. Here, it offers the MSR-ACC/TAE25 dataset of
76,879 total atomization energies obtained at the CCSD(T)/CBS level via the
W1-F12 thermochemical protocol. The dataset is constructed to exhaustively
cover chemical space for all elements up to argon by enumerating and sampling
chemical graphs, thus avoiding bias towards any particular subspace of the
chemical space (such as drug-like, organic, or experimentally observed
molecules). With this first dataset in MSR-ACC, we enable data-driven
approaches for developing predictive computational chemistry methods with
unprecedented accuracy and scope.

</details>

Conclusion: 本文提出的方法为研究光化学反应中价层和核层电子的动力学提供了新的视角和精准工具。通过分析CS₂分子的例子，深化了对预 dissociation机制的理解，特别是在价层电子和几何变化对反应动力学中的关键步骤的调节作用。该研究为类似的复杂反应的动力学研究提供了范例。

### [123] [Resonant helical dichroism in twisted dielectric metastructures](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14173)
*Yiyuan Wang,Chi Li,Haoyi Yu,Stefan A. Maier,Jinhui Shi,Haoran Ren,Kirill Koshelev*

Main category: physics.optics

TL;DR: 这项研究利用旋转的光束和细粒状的微纳米结构实现了强_resonant 的环形和线性二色体特性。通过旋转死lectric元结构，研究者成功地实现了对光束自旋角动量的不同值的精确调控，为分子表征、光学成像、非线性光学和光数据存储等应用提供了新的工具。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 光子的自旋角动量结构在分子表征和光学成像中有重要作用，目前对于高光强的光子自旋角动量具有挑战性的研究较少，鉴于此，研究者试图通过细粒状的微纳米结构和旋转的多模态光子场实现对光子自旋角动量的精确控制，从而提升环形和线性二色体特性。

Method: 研究者设计和实现了由旋转的Si微粒阵列组成的死电介质元结构，利用这些元结构的高质量因数（约几十倍）和旋转的光子自旋角动量使得光子场能够与材料的共振耦合，从而实现了多值光子自旋角动量的强光致强线性和环形二色体特性。

Result: 通过实验证实实现了强_resonant 的线性和环形二色体特性，目标值为光子自旋角动量值1到3的多值。

Conclusion: 该研究成功实现了对光子自旋角动量的精确调控，为未来在分子表征、光学成像、非线性光学和光数据存储等领域的高性能应用提供了强有力的工具。

Abstract: Circular dichroism, arising from interactions with light fields of opposite
spin angular momentum, has become a fundamental tool for molecular
characterization. Meanwhile, helical dichroism (HD) - the dichroic response to
vortex beams carrying opposite orbital angular momentum (OAM) - offers an
alternative approach for probing chiral molecules and photonic structures.
Previous demonstrations of HD have been limited to non-resonant light-matter
interactions with chiral micro- and nanostructures, leaving the realization of
resonance helical dichroism largely unexplored. Here, we present the design and
implementation of twisted dielectric metastructures, composed of an array of
rotated silicon trimer nanostructures harnessing nonlocal photonic modes with a
high quality factor of several dozen that enable strong resonant HD for OAM
values up to $10$. We experimentally demonstrate resonantly enhanced HD for
strongly focused OAM beams with the magnitude of topological charges from $1$
to $3$. Our findings pave the way for resonant nanophotonics involving OAM
beams, unlocking the full potential of structured light for applications in
molecular sensing, optical imaging, nonlinear optics, and optical data storage.

### [125] [GHz spiking neuromorphic photonic chip with in-situ training](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.14272)

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 随着人工智能的发展，光子神经计算作为一种生物启发的计算模式，具有更低的能耗和更高的计算速度。因此，研究这样的硬件芯片具有重要的意义，可以推动相关领域的技术进步。

Method: 该研究采用了基于互补金属氧化半导体平台的光子架构，设计了一个具备高效事件驱动和无帧处理能力的光子渗流神经网络芯片。利用光电子学技术实现了高频率的非线性激活，结合监督学习的自适应连接调整，以及基于人眼-retina的冲动编码，解决了空间时间和能量效率问题。

Result: 该PSNN芯片实现了KTH视频识别数据集80%的准确率，处理速度是传统方法的100倍，且不需要帧，具有低延迟和高吞吐量。

Conclusion: 这篇文章的主要贡献是一台开创性的光子渗流神经网络芯片，展示了先进的神经计算架构和高效的处理能力，为实现高效、智能的神经计算系统奠定了基础。

Abstract: Neuromorphic photonic computing represents a paradigm shift for
next-generation machine intelligence, yet critical gaps persist in emulating
the brain's event-driven, asynchronous dynamics,a fundamental barrier to
unlocking its full potential. Here, we report a milestone advancement of a
photonic spiking neural network (PSNN) chip, the first to achieve full-stack
brain-inspired computing on a complementary metal oxide
semiconductor-compatible silicon platform. The PSNN features transformative
innovations of gigahertz-scale nonlinear spiking dynamics,in situ learning
capacity with supervised synaptic plasticity, and informative event
representations with retina-inspired spike encoding, resolving the
long-standing challenges in spatiotemporal data integration and
energy-efficient dynamic processing. By leveraging its frame-free, event-driven
working manner,the neuromorphic optoelectronic system achieves 80% accuracy on
the KTH video recognition dataset while operating at ~100x faster processing
speeds than conventional frame-based approaches. This work represents a leap
for neuromorphic computing in a scalable photonic platform with low latency and
high throughput, paving the way for advanced applications in real-time dynamic
vision processing and adaptive decision-making, such as autonomous vehicles and
robotic navigation.

Method: 提出了一种并行光学矩阵乘法方法，称为POMMM，通过单光束传播实现全并行张量处理，解决现有光方法的不足，通过缩放性能、计算能力和效率的提升来提高计算能力。

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: This paper addresses the challenge of improving emission intensity and decay control in hBN for scalable quantum photonics. The proposed method could be a significant advancement in the field.

Method: The study uses thermal dewetting to integrate plasmonic nanocavities with quantum emitters in hBN nanoflakes, creating two configurations: AgNPs on bare hBN and hybrid nanocavities on Au/SiO2 substrates. The method does not require deterministic positioning and achieves enhanced light emission efficiency.

Result: The integration increases photoluminescence intensity up to 100-fold with improved uniformity and emitter lifetimes. FDTD simulations and time-resolved PL measurements validate the size-dependent effects and cavity interactions.

Abstract: Defect-based quantum emitters in hexagonal boron nitride (hBN) are promising

intensity and controlling the decay dynamics remain significant challenges.
This study demonstrates a low-cost, scalable fabrication approach to integrate
plasmonic nanocavities with defect-based quantum emitters in hBN nanoflakes.
Using the thermal dewetting process, we realize two distinct configurations:
stochastic Ag nanoparticles (AgNPs) on hBN flakes and hybrid plasmonic
nanocavities formed by AgNPs on top of hBN flakes supported on gold/silicon
dioxide (Au/SiO2) substrates. While AgNPs on bare hBN yield up to a two-fold

deterministic positioning. Finite-difference time-domain (FDTD) simulations and

dynamics and cavity-emitter interactions. Our versatile solution overcomes key
quantum photonic device development challenges, including material integration,
emission intensity optimization, and spectral multiplexity. Future work will
explore potential applications in integrated photonic circuits hosting on-chip
quantum systems and hBN-based label-free single-molecule detection through such
quantum nanoantennas.

Abstract: We present and compare three approaches for accurately retrieving
depth-resolved temperature distributions within materials from their
thermal-radiation spectra, based on: (1) a nonlinear equation solver

fused-silica window heated on a temperature-controlled stage. Our results
demonstrate that the DNN-based method consistently outperforms conventional
numerical techniques on both synthetic and experimental data, providing a
